<HI>TIRUNA1VUKKARAS4A(R). He was a S4aivaite like
<>Tirujn5a1nasambandhar (Refer above) and a disciple also
<>of the latter. He was born in the village of Tiruva1mur
<>in South Arcot district. His father was Pugalana1r and
<>mother Madiniya1r both of whom were Vella1las. They
<>got a daughter named Tilakavatiya1r and a son named
<>Marulni1kkiya1r. It was this Marulni1kkiya1r who became
<>famous as Tiruna1vukkara ar. This siddha who acquired
<>divine knowledge has composed 4900 songs in praise
<>of S4iva of which only 312 are in use now. [Page790-b+ 64]
<HI>TI1RTHA. A holy place. Even from very ancient times
<>the people of Bha1rata believed in the sacredness of holy
<>places and they considered a pilgirmage to holy places
<>as a part and parcel of their life. Almost all the Pura1n2as
<>have praised the greatness of holy places.
<NI>It is not true that all those who visit holy places and
<>bathe in the sacred ponds there would get salvation. In
<>Chapter 11 of Padma Pura1n2a it is stated thus:
<NI>He would get salvation whose limbs, mind, knowledge,
<>austerity and fame are under his own control. He who
<>lives clean in body, without egoism, contented and never
<>accepting gifts for services done would get salvation by
<>visiting holy places. He who would fast if he did not
<>get food, whose organs of sense are all under control
<>would get salvation if he visits holy places. He who is
<>righteous, free from anger, treats all animate objects
<>like himself would get salvation if he visits holy place.
<NI>Once the great sage Cyavana told Prahla1da thus: “Only
<>those who are pure in heart would get the benefit of
<>visiting sacred places. It is a sin for others to do pilgrim-
<>age. The banks of Gan3ga1 are crowded with villages
<>and cities. Many types of people like Parayas, Fisher-
<>men, Van3gas, Khasas, Huns and Mlecchas live there.
<>They bathe in the holy river and drink the holy water,
<>but they do not get salvation because their mind and
<>heart are not clean.” (4th Skandha, Devi1 Bha1gavata).

<HI>T2IT2T2IBHASARAS. A sacred pond near the a1s4rama of
<>Va1lmi1ki. There is a story about this pond. Once
<>a water-fowl lived there with his mate. One day
<>the male fowl went out for food and as he was
<>returning home he found a few other water-fowls going
<>that way and the male fowl suspected the chastity of his
<>wife. The male fowl decided to abandon his mate and
<>the innocent shefowl prayed to the As2t2adikpa1lakas for
<>help. The As2t2adikpa1lakas instantly appeared there and
<>made a pond and said that if the she-fowl could reach
<>from one shore to the other without getting herself
<>drowned she must be treated as chaste. The she-fowl
<>was accordingly put into the waters and asked to swim
<>to the other shore which she did without any accident.
<>From that day onwards the pon2d was called T2it2t2ibha-
<>saras. (Tit2t2ibha = water fowl. Saras = pond).
<NI>When Si1ta1 came to the a1s4rama of Va1lmi1ki after being
<>abandoned by S4ri1 Ra1ma, Va1lmi1ki wanted to test her
<>chastity. So the sages asked Si1ta1 to enter the pond and
<>reach the other shore. “Oh goddess of Earth, if even in [Page791-a+ 64]
<>my dreams no other person than my husband has
<>entered my thoughts, let me reach the other shore safe.”
<>So saying Si1ta1 entered the water and the goddess of
<>Earth placed her in her lap and took her to the other
<>shore. Si1ta1 did not get even wet. All the sages called her
<>‘Maha1sa1dhvi1’ meaning supremely chaste woman.
<>(Taran3ga 1, Alan3ka1ravati1lambaka, Katha1saritsa1gara).

<HI>TOLA. A great satirical poet of the Malaya1lam Litera-
<>ture. A great humorist, Sanskrit scholar and actor, he
<>was minister to Bha1skara Ravi Varma1 who was ruler
<>of Kerala during the period from 978 to 1027 A.D.
<>According to Kodun3gallur Kun5jikkuttan Tampura1n, a
<>great Sanskrit scholar and poet, Tola was born in
<>Kondolin5n5a1ru in the village of Aira1n2ikkulam near Ad2u1r
<>in Cochin in a Nambu1diri family. His original name
<>was Ni1lakan2t2ha. When he was a young man, he was
<>ostracised from his community for having had illicit
<>connections with a low-caste servant-maid named
<>Cakki1. He was wearing then a deerskin belt (Tol) on
<>his body as the usual mark of Brahmaca1rins (bachelors)
<>and he threw it away of his own accord earning for him
<>the name Tola. There is another version that Tola is
<>the decayed form of ‘Atula’ meaning matchless. He
<>was mainly interested in writing funny ridicules. There
<>are many such poems now available believed to be
<>those of Tola.

<HI>TRIJAT2A (GA1RGYA). A sage. Though he was a sage

<HI>TRIKU1T2A. A mountain. There are twenty mountains
<>on the four sides of Maha1meru including Triku1t2a.

<>Ra1van2a, was at the top of Triku1t2a. Maha1meru is at the
<>north of Bha1rata. Lan3ka1 is to the south of Bha1rata.
<>Then how is it possible for Lan3ka1 to be on the top of
<>Triku1t2a?
<NI>There is a story to substantiate this belief. Once there
<>arose a quarrel between Va1suki and Va1yubhagava1n
<>and they decided to find out who between the two was
<>more powerful. Va1suki went and lay wound round
<>Maha1meru so tightly that even Va1yu (air) could not
<>enter it. Va1yu got enraged and broke into a cyclone
<>shaking the whole world. Even Maha1meru began to
<>shake but Va1suki lay unaffected. The Cyclone began to
<>increase in vigour and the devas were frightened and
<>they went to Maha1vis2n2u accompanied by S4iva and
<>Brahma1. After hearing their story Vis2n2u called Va1suki
<>and Va1yu to his side and commanded them to stop the
<>quarrel. Va1suki then unwound a part of his winding
<>and that was from Triku1t2a. At once Va1yu entered
<>there and separating Triku1t2a from other parts carried
<>it away and dropped it in the southern sea. It fell to
<>the south of the southern end of Bha1rata. Lan3ka1 is the
<>city built on it by the celebrated architect,
<>Vis4vakarman.

<HI>TRIPURA. A phantom city built by Maya.
<NI>1) {%Origin.%} Kas4yapa Mahars2i son of Mari1ci and grand-
<>son of Brahma1 had many wives. Of them Aditi got the
<>first place and Diti the second place. Both of them were
<>daughters of Daks2a Devas were born of Aditi and the
<>asuras were born of Diti. Armies of asuras under the
<>leadership of S4u1rapadma, Sim3havaktra, Ta1raka1sura,
<>Gomukha, Hiran2ya1ks2a, and Hiran2yakas4ipu gave immense
<>trouble to the devas. The devas joined together under
<>the leadership of Indra and fought the asuras. The
<>nectar received from the ocean of Milk always made
<>the devas the conquerors. When Subrahman2ya slew
<>Ta1raka1sura the asuras became very weak. [Page793-b+ 65]
<>At this stage Kamala1ks2a, Ta1raka1ks2a and Vidyunma1li1,
<>sons of Ta1raka1sura, did severe penance and made Brahma1
<>appear before them. They demanded a boon that they
<>would never be killed by anybody in any of the three
<>worlds. Brahma1 told them to ask any boon other than
<>that. Then they said: “Great Lord, we must live in
<>three cities and then roam about freely in the three
<>worlds by your grace. Every thousand years all the
<>three of us should join together at a place with our
<>cities. After that meeting, we should separate and roam
<>about freely for another thousand years. If at all there
<>is death for us, it should occur only when we three
<>are together and that also by one arrow.” Brahma1
<>granted the boon and disappeared.
<NI>The asuras then approached Maya and asked him to
<>construct three separate cities for them. Maya built
<>three wonderful cities. One was with gold, another
<>with silver and the third with iron. Ta1raka1ks2a took
<>the golden one, Kamala1ks2a took the silver one and
<>Vidyunma1li1 took the iron one. The asuras started
<>living in these cities. The three puras were respectively
<>in Svarga, A1ka1s4a and the Earth. But each city had the
<>power to travel to any other place at will. The power
<>of controlling these cities was given to Ba1n2a. Hiran2ya-
<>kas4ipu's son was Prahla1da. Prahla1da's son was Viro-
<>cana. Maha1bali was Virocana's son and Ba1n2a was
<>Maha1bali's son (Chapter 14, Padma Pura1n2a). All these
<>three cities together were named Tripura.
<NI>2) {%Mr2tasan5ji1vani1 Va1pi1.%} (The life giving tank). Even
<>with the existence of Tripura the asuras began to die in
<>numbers and the Tripuras thought of a way to escape
<>from this calamity. Hari, son of Ta1raka1sura, did penance
<>and made Brahma1 appear before him in person.
<>According to a request from Hari Brahma1 made Maya
<>build a tank wonderful in nature. Brahma1 filled the
<>tank with nectar. If any asura died, it was enough if he
<>was dipped in the tank and the dead asura would soon
<>come to life with added strength and vigour. Asuras
<>became immortal since this and the Tripuras started
<>teasing the devas and men with increased ferocity.
<NI>3) {%Consultation with S4iva.%} The aggrieved devas approach-
<>ed Brahma1 and finding him incapable of helping took
<>him to S4iva. S4iva heard everything and assured them
<>that he would kill them when they next met together at
<>the end of a thousand years.
<NI>4) {%S4iva makes preparations.%} As a first step to the slaughter
<>of the Tripuras, S4iva sent Na1rada to Tripura. Na1rada
<>by his unusual spiritual powers made the asura women
<>feel more and more attached to the devas. S4iva at that
<>time thinking about the convenience for a fight with
<>the Tripuras came and settled down on the shores of
<>the river Narmada1. That was how Narmada1 became
<>a holy river. (Chapter 13, Padma Pura1n2a).
<NI>S4iva had to make grand preparations for a fight with
<>the Tripuras. He invoked half the strength of the devas
<>to himself to make S4ivas4akti (Javelin of S4iva) greater
<>than Asuras4akti. The devas made Vis4vakarma1 construct
<>a special chariot for S4iva. On the banks of the river
<>Narmada1 at a place which became renowned as
<>Mahes4vara S4iva stayed for a thousand years thinking
<>about the fight with the Tripuras. He made the mount-
<>ain of Mandara his bow, Va1suki, the string and
<>Vis2n2u his arrow. He installed Agni at the tip and Va1yu
<>at the bottom of the arrow. Four devas stood as horses
<>to his chariot. The earth itself was the chariot and all [Page794-a+ 65]
<>the animate and inanimate objects of the devaloka
<>arrayed at different parts of the chariot. On the wheels
<>stood the As4vini1devas and Cakrapa1n2i stayed on the
<>axle. Gandharvas took places on the spokes. Indra
<>stayed on the bow and Vais4ravan2a on the arrow. Yama
<>took his place on the right hand and the dreadful Ka1la
<>on the left hand. Brahma1 acted as the charioteer.
<NI>Equipped thus, S4iva stayed in the godly chariot for a
<>thousand years. When the three cities joined together
<>in the sky S4iva split the cities by his three forked spike.
<>Then he sent an arrow to the cities. Bad omens began
<>to appear in Tripura. People became lifeless in the
<>cities. Soon an arrow from S4iva burnt the cities and
<>the Tripuras were burnt to death. (7th Skandha,
<>Bha1gavata; Chapters 31 to 34, Padma Pura1n2a; Chapters
<>33 and 34, Karn2a Parva).

<HI>TRIS4AN3KU I. (SATYAVRATA, MATAN3GA). A
<>celebrated King of the Solar dynasty.
<NI>1) {%Genealogy.%} Descending in order from Brahma1--
<>Mari1ci--Kas4yapa--Vivasva1n--Vaivasvata Manu--
<>Iks2va1ku--Vikuks2i--S4as4a1da--Puran5jaya (Kakutstha)--
<>Anenas--Pr2thula1s4va--Prasenajit, Yuvana1s4va--Ma1n-
<>dha1ta1--Purukutsa--Trasadasyu--Anaran2ya--Haryas4va
<>Vasumanas--Sudhanva1--Trayya1run2a--Satyavrata
<>(Tris4an3ku).
<NI>2) {%Father discards him.%} When Satyavrata grew up he
<>became a lewd, lustful imprudent man. One day while he
<>was leading such a contemptuous life, a marriage was
<>being conducted in a brahmin house. Guests had
<>assembled, the bridegroom had come and the ceremony
<>was about to start when Satyavrata entered the
<>marriage hall and carried away by force the bride to
<>the shock of all those present there. Some of the Brahmin
<>guests immediately went to Trayya1run2a and told him
<>what a shameful crime his son had committed. The enrag-
<>ed father at once sent Satyavrata out from the palace.
<>Satyavrata left the country altogether and went and
<>stayed in a colony of harijans. Though he lived with
<>those low-caste people he did not adopt their mode of
<>living. He went out daily to the forests with his bow
<>and arrow and made his food. He never felt any
<>animosity towards his father who had thus sent him out
<>from his country. He thought thus “Of course, my father
<>got terribly angry when he heard the complaints of the
<>Brahmins and in that mood punished me thus, though
<>the punishment was a bit too much. But our family
<>preceptor Vasis2t2ha, who knows everything, who is a
<>moralist and a righteous man, who has the knowledge
<>and authority to prescribe atonement for all sins, did
<>severe punishment. That was very hard.” As he thought
<>more about it in this vein, he felt a great hatred towards
<>Vasis2t2ha.
<NI>3) {%Satyavrata and Vis4va1mitra's family.%} When his only
<>son Satyavrata was turned out from the family, King
<>Trayya1run2a was greatly distressed. He went to the [Page794-b+ 64]
<>forests to do penance to get another son. At that time
<>the country did not have rains for twelve successive
<>years as a punishment for the King for sending out his
<>son. The people suffered much. Among the people who
<>were suffering were the wife and children of Vis4va1mitra.
<>Vis4va1mitra at that time had gone to the shores of river
<>Kaus4iki1 for doing penance. Vis4va1mitra's family consist-
<>ing of his wife and three sons during that famine lived
<>in hunger. At last the mother decided to sell the middle
<>son and buy food with the money received by the sale.
<>She put a rope made of darbha grass round the neck
<>of the boy and took him to the market. On the way
<>Satyavrata saw them and on hearing their sad story told
<>them not to sell the child. He assured them that he
<>would take care of them till the return of Vis4va1mitra.
<>He removed the darbha rope from the child's neck and
<>the child got the name of Ga1lava from that time on-
<>wards. (Gala=neck). He promised them he would
<>daily place enough meat at the foot of a tree near the
<>a1s4rama. True to his promise, he hunted in the forests
<>and brought to the foot of the tree fresh flesh of deer or
<>hare or boar and also fresh fruits. The family lived
<>happily because of him.
<NI>4) {%Curse of Vasis2t2ha and the name of Tris4an3ku.%} When
<>Trayya1run2a went to the forests to do penance, it was
<>Vasis2t2ha who was managing the affairs of the palace.
<>The heir-apparent Satyavrata lived in the hut of a
<>can2d2a1la. Every minute Satyavrata's hatred towards
<>Vasis2t2ha increased in strength. One day Satyavrata did
<>not get any game even after a day's hunting and at
<>dusk he happened to reach the a1s4rama of Vasis2t2ha
<>where he saw Nandini1, the beloved cow of the sage,
<>grazing by the side of the a1s4rama. Anger, desire and
<>hunger made him imprudent and without thinking of
<>the consequences Satyavrata killed Nandini1 and after
<>eating enough to appease his hunger took the rest to
<>feed the family of Vis4va1mitra. The wife of Vis4va1mitra
<>little knowing that it was cow's flesh cooked it and
<>ate it.
<NI>That night when Vasis2t2ha came to the a1s4rama he found
<>Nandini1 missing and he went in search of it. After some
<>time the sage knew that Satyavrata had killed and eaten
<>it. The enraged sage called Satyavrata to his side and
<>cursed him thus “You will from today become a
<>can2d2a1la. Three s4an3kus (sins) namely wrath of a father,
<>abduction of another man's wife and consumption of
<>cow's flesh will give you life-long trouble and thus you
<>will earn a name, Tris4an3ku (Three s4an3kus). Instantly
<>Satyavrata became a can2d2a1la and started roaming
<>about in the streets.
<NI>5) {%Tris4an3ku becomes King.%} Tris4an3ku, distressed at heart
<>by a father's wrath and a Guru's curse walked about
<>aimlessly in the forests. He expressed his desire to the
<>r2s2is and Brahmins to do a ya1ga and get himself absolved
<>of all his sins. But nobody was willing to help a wretch-
<>ed man cursed and abandoned by both his father and
<>his Guru. Feeling desperate, he decided to commit
<>suicide. He made a great fire-pit and prepared himself
<>to jump into it. Before doing that he prayed to the
<>goddess and when the goddess knew that his devotee
<>would jump into the fire and become ashes, she appear-
<>ed before him in person and said thus: “Son, why do
<>you try to jump into the fire? Your father has become
<>old and day after tomorrow he will crown you as King [Page795-a+ 65]
<>and then go to the forests to do penance. Look, there
<>comes your father's minister to take you to the palace.”
<>When the goddess disappeared Satyavrata returned to
<>his a1s4rama in a pensive mood. Na1rada went and in-
<>formed the king of everything that happened in the
<>forest and the king immediately sent his ministers to
<>fetch Satyavrata to the palace. When Satyavrata came
<>the king crowned him as king and then went to the
<>forests for penance.
<NI>6) {%Satyavrata becomes Can2d2a1la again.%} Satyavrata ruled the
<>country for a long time. He was a pious ruler, devoted
<>to god and soon he developed a desire to go to heaven
<>with his mortal body. He approached Vasis2t2ha first
<>for this purpose. But the family preceptor told him
<>there was nothing in the s4a1stras about any ya1ga which
<>could help one to go bodily to heaven. Disappointed
<>he approached the sons of Vasis2t2ha who ridiculed him
<>when he told them of his queer desire. Tris4an3ku got
<>angry and left them saying “Let me see whether there
<>are others in this country who could send me bodily to
<>heaven.” Those arrogant words annoyed Vasis2t2ha and
<>his sons and they cursed him and made him a can2d2a1la
<>again. Tris4an3ku thereafter did not return to the palace,
<>but went to the forests to live there. He knew if he
<>returned to the palace as a can2d2a1la he would not be
<>recognised by his wife and children.
<NI>Haris4candra, son of Tris4an3ku, heard about the curse on
<>his father and sent the ministers to fetch his father to
<>the palace. But Tris4an3ku did not come back and so the
<>ministers made Haris4candra the king of Ayodhya1.
<NI>7) {%Vis4va1mitra meets Tris4an3ku.%} When Haris4candra became
<>king, Tris4an3ku was living in Amba1vana (forest of Amba1)
<>as a great devotee of the goddess. It was at that time
<>that Vis4va1mitra returned home after his penance. Vis4va1-
<>mitra enquired of his wife how they managed to live
<>during the great famine. Then Satyavati1, wife of Vis4va1-
<>mitra, told him the whole story of how Satyavrata helped
<>them, why he killed Nandini1, Vasis2t2ha's cow, and how
<>they ate cow's flesh, how Satyavrata was cursed to be a
<>can2d2a1la, how he was called back as king and how he was
<>at that time living in Amba1vana. The eyes of Vis4va1-
<>mitra1 became wet when he heard the sorrowful story
<>and he decided to end the can2d2a1latva (state of being a
<>can2d2a1la) of Satyavrata. He went straight to Amba1vana
<>and met Tris4an3ku there.
<NI>8) {%Tris4an3ku Svarga (Heaven of Tris4an3ku).%} Vis4va1mitra pro-
<>mised Tris4an3ku that he would send him to heaven bodily
<>and made preparations for a ya1ga. No other sage par-
<>took in the ya1ga because of instructions from Vasis2t2ha.
<>But undaunted, Vis4va1mitra conducted the ya1ga alone
<>and, as the power of his performances increased, Tri-
<>s4an3ku started rising bodily from earth slowly and soon
<>rose up to heaven. When the devas found a Can2d2a1la
<>standing with his physical body before the gates of
<>heaven, they ran to Indra and told him. Indra got
<>angry and pushed him out from heaven and Tris4an3ku
<>came falling down with his head turned downwards to
<>the earth. Tris4an3ku cried loudly calling Vis4va1mitra
<>by name. When Vis4va1mitra, hearing the noise, looked
<>up he saw poor Tris4an3ku descending fast from heaven
<>with his head turned upside down. Vis4va1mitra's anger
<>knew no bounds and he roared aloud “Let Tris4an3ku
<>stay where he is now.” Tris4an3ku stopped in mid-air.
<>Indra did not allow Tris4an3ku to come up and Vis4va1-
<>mitra did not allow him to come down. Indra then made [Page795-b+ 64]
<>a separate heaven for Tris4an3ku below original
<>heaven. Then Vis4va1mitra started to create another Indra
<>and devas for the new heaven. The devas were frightened
<>and Indra then approached Vis4va1mitra and requested
<>him to desist from his attempt to make duplicate devas
<>promising him that he would give Tris4an3ku a seat in
<>his heaven itself. Vis4va1mitra agreed to it. At once
<>Indra brought a golden Vima1na and took him bodily to
<>heaven. (Sargas 57 to 59, Ba1laka1n2d2a, Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a
<>7th Skandha, Devi1 Bha1gavata; 9th Skandha, Bha1gavata;
<>Chapter 13, Harivam3s4a; Sundara Ka1n2d2a, Kamba
<>Ra1ma1yan2a; Chapter 71, A1di Parva; Chapter 12, Sabha1
<>Parva).

<HI>TRIS4IRAS I. A demon who was a friend of Ra1van2a. The

<HI>TRIS4IRAS II (VIS4VARU1PA). Once there was a celebrat-
<>ed Praja1pati of name Tvas2t2a1. Though he was of a pious
<>nature interested in the welfare of Brahmins, he hated
<>Indra. He thought of destroying Indra somehow. With

<>three heads and so he was called Tris4iras (Tri=Three
<>S4iras--head) also. He could use his three heads for
<>three different purposes at a time. He would drink wine
<>with one head and mutter the Veda-mantras by another
<>head and see the world by the third.
<NI>Even from boyhood he disliked worldly pleasures and,
<>abandoning even food, started to do penance. During
<>the hot season he would sit amidst fire and during the
<>cold season he would sit in water to do penance. He
<>would stand with his head down and do penance. The
<>penance of Tris4iras was so severe that Indra began to
<>get frightened. He sent celestial maidens to stop the
<>penance but all the attempts proved futile before that
<>great ascetic. Then Indra himself riding on Aira1vata
<>went and killed the sage by his Vajra1yudha. Indra
<>feared whether Tris4iras would come to life again and
<>wreak vengeance on him. So he ordered a carpenter
<>standing nearby to bring to him the three heads separat-
<>ed from the body. The carpenter cut off the heads from
<>the body and as each head fell to the ground several
<>kinds of birds were found escaping from it. From the
<>head which used to mutter Vedic mantras rose the
<>Kapin5jala birds; from the head used for drinking wine
<>rose Kalapin3ga birds and from the third rose the Tittiri
<>birds. When the birds thus rose to the air Indra was
<>convinced that Tris4iras was dead and he went away
<>See under Vis4varu1pa. (6th Skandha, Devi1 Bha1gavata).

<HI>TRITA.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} A son of the sage Gautama. He

<NI>1) {%Grandfather of Vis4ravas.%} Vis4ravas, father of Ra1van2a

<NI>Once the sage Pulastya was doing penance in a seclud-

<NI>2) {%How he cursed Hanu1ma1n.%} Once Hanu1ma1n caught

<>knew by his divine powers that the perpetrator of that

<>he would lose all his divine powers forthwith.

<>would regain his powers at the time of his going in
<>search of Si1ta1 when another member of his species

<>Mahendra mountain on the shores of Bha1rata. Ja1mba-
<>va1n, a mighty monkey chief called Hanu1ma1n to his
<>side and made him understand the great powers latent
<>in him. From that moment onwards Hanu1ma1n regained
<>his lost powers and became his old self. (See under

<>the gate-keepers did not allow him to enter the palace
<>premises. (S4loka 17, Chapter 51, Sabha1 Parva).
<HI>TRYAMBAKA. One of the Eka1das4a Rudras (eleven
<>Rudras). See under Eka1das4arudra).
<HI>TUGRA. A King extolled in the R2gveda. This King
<>sent his son Bhujyu with a large army by sea to
<>conquer his enemies in dvi1pa1ntara. When they were a
<>long distance away from the shore the boats carrying
<>them capsized in a storm and the prince and army
<>were drowned in the sea. The prince then prayed to
<>the A vini1devas and they saved him and his army from
<>the sea and sent them back to the palace. Those boats
<>could travel both in the sea and the air. (Su1kta 116,
<>Man2d2ala 1, R2gveda, Anuva1ka 17).
<HI>TUHARA. A soldier of Subrahman2ya. (Chapter 45,
<>S4alya Parva).
<HI>TUHUN2D2A. A demon. This demon was born to
<>Kas4yapa of his wife Danu. (Chapter 65, A1di Parva).
<NI>Accompanied by Ta1raka1sura this demon once attacked
<>Subrahman2ya. Tuhun2d2a threw an iron mace against
<>Gan2apati who blocked his chariot. By a single stone of
<>Gan2apati, the diamond-studded mace of the demon
<>broke into six pieces. When he found his mace gone
<>the demon caught hold of Gan2apati and beat him with
<>a spiked club on his forehead. Gan2apati cut him with
<>his weapon (Axe) ‘Ven2mazhu’. The demon fell to the
<>ground in two pieces but still his hold on Gan2apati
<>was not released. Gan2apati tried his best but could not
<>loosen the hold. Then Kun2d2odara, a leader of the
<>attendants of Gan2apati smashed the hands of Tuhun2d2a
<>with an iron mace. Tuhun2d2a was killed thus. (Chapter
<>65, Va1yu Pura1n2a).
<NI>This Tuhun2d2a was born in his next life in the world as
<>a King called Sena1bindu. (S4loka 19, Chapter 67, A1di
<>Parva).

<HI>TULA1PURUS2ADA1NA. See under Meruda1na. [Page797-b+ 64]
<HI>TULASI1. (Holy Basil plant.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} Tulasi1 is a plant held most
<>sacred by the Hindus. There is a Pura1n2ic background for
<>Tulasi1 attaining this spiritualistic importance. In fact
<>it is Maha1laks2mi1, wife of Vis2n2u, who had herself taken
<>the form of Tulasi1. There is a story about it in Devi
<>Bha1gavata.
<NI>2) {%The curse of Sarasvati1.%} Sarasvati1, Gan3ga1 and
<>Laks2mi1 were all, in the beginning, wives of Maha1vis2n2u.
<>The Lord loved all the three equally. One day all the
<>four were sitting together when Gan3ga1 sent lustful
<>glances at Vis2n2u which was immediately noticed by
<>both Sarasvati1 and Laks2mi1. Sarasvati1 got angry and
<>rising up caught hold of the hair of Gan3ga1 and dragged
<>her to the ground. Laks2mi1 then caught hold of Saras-
<>vati1 to prevent further assault but Sarasvati1 then
<>poured all her rage on Laks2mi1 and cursed her to be
<>born as a plant on earth. Gan3ga1devi1 could not bear
<>this and she cursed Sarasvati1 to be born as a river on
<>earth. Sarasvati1 retorted with a curse that Gan3ga1 also
<>would be born as a river. When the whole tumult was
<>over Vis2n2u called Laks2mi1 to his side and said--“Oh
<>Devi1, do not worry. Things have happened as predes-
<>tined. You go and be born as the daughter of Dharma-
<>dhvaja and grow up there. From there by divine grace
<>you will be transformed into a plant sacred enough to
<>make all the three worlds pure. That plant will be
<>named Tulasi1. When you will be thus living as Tulasi1,
<>a demon named S4an3khacu1d2a with part of my virile
<>strength will be born and he will marry you. Then you
<>can come back to me. The holy river Padma1vati1 will
<>also be another form of your spirit.”
<NI>3) {%The story of Dharmadhvaja.%} Who was this Dharma-
<>dhvaja to whom was born Maha1laks2mi1 as a daughter?
<>In times of old there was a Manu called Daks2asa1varn2i
<>who was extremely virtuous and a part of Vis2n2u. Des-
<>cending from Daks2asa1varn2i were Brahmasa1varn2i-
<>Dharmasa1varn2i-Rudrasa1varn2i-Devasa1varn2i-Indrasa1varn2i
<>Vr2s2adhvaja. This last named was a great devotee of
<>S4iva and because of his great affection for this devotee
<>S4iva lived a whole period of a devayuga in the a1s4rama
<>of Vr2s2adhvaja. King Vr2s2adhvaja by an edict prohibited
<>the worship of any other deity than S4iva in his country.
<>Even the worship of Maha1laks2mi1 ordained by the Vedas
<>during the month of Bha1dra (September) became ex-
<>tinct. All Ya1gas and worship of Vis2n2u came to a stop.
<>Su1rya (Sun-god) got angry at this belittling of other
<>gods than S4iva and cursed the King Vr2s2adhvaja that he
<>would cease to be prosperous. S4iva did not like it and
<>he went to punish Su1rya holding his trident in his
<>hand. Su1rya was frightened and he approached his
<>father Kas4yapa. Kas4yapa and Su1rya went to Brahma1
<>and acquainted him with all details. Brahma1 also was
<>helpless in the matter and so all the three of them went
<>to Maha1vis2n2u. They prostrated before Vis2n2u and told
<>him all. At that time S4iva also came there. Addressing
<>all of them Vis2n2u said “Oh, Devas, within this half an
<>hour twentyone yugas have passed by on the earth. He
<>about whom you have come to speak to me is dead and
<>gone. Even his son Rathadhvaja is dead. The latter
<>has two sons named Dharmadhvaja and Kus4adhvaja.
<>They are dull and splendourless now because of the curse
<>of Su1rya and are now worshipping Laks2mi1.” Saying
<>thus Vis2n2u disappeared. [Page798-a+ 63]
<NI>4) {%Birth of Tulasi1.%} Dharmadhvaja and Kus4adhvaja
<>did penance to propitiate Maha1laks2mi1. Kus4adhvaja
<>had a wife named Ma1la1vati1. She bore a daughter named
<>Vedavati1. Si1ta1, wife of S4ri1 Ra1ma, was a rebirth of this
<>Vedavati1.
<NI>King Dharmadhvaja had a wife named Ma1dhavi1. Maha1-
<>laks2mi1 entered her womb as an embryo and after a hund-
<>red years Ma1dhavi1 gave birth to a daughter. Even at the
<>time of birth the child looked like a matured girl and was
<>extremely pretty. She was therefore, called Tulasi1, meaning
<>matchless. (Tula=match). This Tulasi1 abandoning all
<>worldly pleasures went to Badarika1s4rama and started doing
<>penance there with the prayer that Maha1vis2n2u should
<>become her husband. She did penance for twentyfour
<>thousand years sitting amidst fire in the hot season and
<>sitting in water in the cold season and taking only
<>fruits and water as food. Then she did penance for ano-
<>ther thirtythousand years eating leaves only, another forty
<>thousand years taking air only as food and another ten
<>thousand years without any food. At this stage Brahma1
<>appeared and asked her the object of her Penance. She
<>replied she wanted Maha1vis2n2u to be her husband.
<>Hearing this Brahma1 said thus--“Devi, you know the
<>cowboy Suda1ma1 born of a part of S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a. That
<>brilliant cowboy has now been born on earth, due to a
<>curse of Ra1dha1, as a demon named S4an3khacu1d2a. He is
<>matchlessly eminent and has once fallen in love with
<>you seeing you at Goloka. You will become his wife and
<>later you can become the wife of Na1ra1yan2a. At that
<>time a part of your divine body will remain on earth as
<>a plant named Tulasi1. Tulasi1 will become the most
<>sacred of all plants, dear to Vis2n2u, and all worship
<>without using Tulasi1 leaves would be ineffective.”
<NI>5) {%Marriage of Tulasi1.%} Due to a curse of Ra1dha1,
<>Suda1ma1, the cowboy, was born on earth as a demon
<>named S4an3khacu1d2a. He did penance sitting at Badarik-
<>a1s4rama and obtained Vis2n2ukavaca. Another object of
<>his was to marry Tulasi1. He obtained a boon from
<>Brahma1 that his death would occur only when the
<>Vis2n2u Kavaca was removed from his body and the
<>chastity of his wife was lost. At that time S4an3khacu1d2a
<>and Tulasi1 met each other in the forests and were
<>married. S4an3khacu1d2a, brilliant and majestic, went
<>about with Tulasi1 in amorous sports creating jealousy
<>even among the devas. His arrogance gave innumer-
<>able troubles to the devas and they along with Brahma1
<>and S4iva approached Maha1vis2n2u for a remedy.
<>Vis2n2u then sent S4iva with his spike to kill S4an3khacu1d2a
<>and he himself started to molest the chastity of his wife
<>Tulasi1. S4an3khacu1da took leave of Tulasi1 to go
<>and fight with S4iva. When Tulasi1 was thus left alone,
<>Maha1vis2n2u in the form of S4an3khacu1d2a approached
<>Tulasi1 and after some preliminary talks entered into
<>sexual acts. Tulasi1 found some difference in the usual
<>sexual methods and suspecting foul play jumped up to
<>curse the impostor. At once Maha1vis2n2u appeared in
<>his true form and said “You have been doing penance
<>for a long time to get me as your husband. Your
<>husband S4an3khacu1d2a was the chief of my Pa1rs2adas,
<>Suda1ma1. It is time for him to go back to Goloka get-
<>ting himself released from the curse. By this time S4iva
<>would have killed him and he would have gone to
<>Goloka as Suda1ma1. You can now abandon your body [Page798-b+ 65]
<>and come with me to Vaikun2t2ha to enjoy life as my
<>wife.
<NI>Your body will decay and become a holy river named
<>Gan2d2aki1; your hair will become Tulasi1 plant the
<>leaves of which will be held sacred in all the three
<>worlds.”
<NI>Tulasi1 then changed herself into the form of Laks2mi1
<>and went to Vaikun2t2ha with Maha1vis2n2u. (9th Skandha,
<>Devi1 Bha1gavata).
<NI>6) {%The greatness of Tulasi1.%} Everything of the Tulasi1
<>plant, leaves, flowers, fruits, roots, twigs, skin and even
<>the soil around is holy. The soul of a dead one whose
<>dead body is cremated using Tulasi1 twigs for firewood
<>would attain a permanent place in Vis2n2uloka. Even
<>great sinners would be absolved of their sins if their
<>dead bodies are cremated with Tulasi1 twigs. If at the
<>time of death one thinks of God and mutters His name
<>and if his dead body is later cremated with Tulasi1
<>twigs, he would have no rebirths. Even he who has
<>done a crore of sins would attain moks2a if at the time
<>of cremating his dead body a piece of Tulasi1 twig is
<>placed at the bottom of the funeral pyre. Just as all
<>waters become pure by the union with Gan3ga1 water,
<>all firewood is made pure by the addition of a small
<>piece of Tulasi1 twig. If the dead body of one is cre-
<>mated using Tulasi1 twigs alone, one's sins for a crore
<>of Kalpa years would be washed away. Yamadu1tas
<>would keep away from one whose dead body is cre-
<>mated with Tulasi1 twigs and servants of Vis2n2u would
<>come near. If a light is burnt for Vis2n2u with a Tulasi1
<>stick it would be equal to burning several lakhs of
<>lights for Vis2n2u. If one makes the Tulasi1 leaves into a
<>paste and smears it on one's body and then worships
<>Vis2n2u for one day, one would be getting the benefit of
<>a hundred ordinary worships and also the benefit of
<>doing a hundred goda1nas. (gifts of cows). (Chapter 24,
<>Padma Pura1n2a).
<HI>TUMBURU I. A Deva Gandharva. He was the best
<>musician among the Gandharvas.
<NI>1) {%Birth.%} Tumburu was the son of Kas4yapa, son of
<>Mari1ci and grandson of Brahma1, born of his wife
<>Pradha1. Of the sons of Kas4yapa the four Gandharva
<>sons, Tumburu, Ba1hu, Ha1ha1 and Hu1hu1 were noted for
<>their sweet and pleasant conversation.
<NI>2) {%Tumburu and the Pa1n2d2avas.%} Maha1bha1rata states
<>about several occasions when Tumburu has shown a
<>special and deep interest in the Pa1n2d2avas. The follow-
<>ing few are of special mention--
<NI>(i) Tumburu attended the Janmotsava of Arjuna.
<>(S4loka 54, Chapter 122, A1di Parva).
<NI>(ii) Once this Gandharva gave Yudhis2t2hira a hundred
<>horses. (S4loka 24, Chapter 52, Sabha1 Parva).
<NI>(iii) Tumburu welcomed Arjuna when the latter went
<>to Devaloka at the invitation of Indra. (Vana Parva,
<>Chapter 43, Verse 14).
<NI>(iv) Once when the Pa1n2d2avas were living incognito in
<>the country of Vira1t2a the Kauravas carried away the
<>cattle of the King. Arjuna in disguise then fought
<>against the Kauravas and Tumburu watched the fight
<>with interest. (S4loka 12, Chapter 56, Vira1t2a Parva).
<NI>(v) Tumburu was present at the As4vamedhaya1ga of
<>Yudhis2t2hira. (S4loka 39, Chapter 88, As4vamedha
<>Parva).
<NI>3) {%How Tumburu was born as Vira1dha.%} When Ra1ma and
<>Laks2man2a were in the forests in exile a demon named [Page799-a+ 64]
<>Vira1dha attacked them. That demon was none other
<>than Tumburu. Once when Tumburu was living in the
<>city of Kubera he committed a sin and Kubera cursed
<>him and made him into a demon. Kubera had then
<>told him that he would get relief from the curse when
<>he was slain by Ra1ma, son of Das4aratha. S4ri1 Ra1ma
<>killed Vira1dha and the latter regaining the form of
<>Tumburu left for Gandharvaloka. (See under Vira1dha).
<NI>4) {%How he cursed Puru1ravas.%} It is found in Katha1saritsa1-
<>gara that the temporary separation which Puru1ravas
<>had from Urvas4i1 was due to a curse by the Gandharva
<>Tumburu.
<NI>After marrying Urvas4i1 Puru1ravas once went to Deva-
<>loka at the invitation of Indra. He was invited to help
<>Indra in his fight against the asuras. Indra celebrated
<>the day on which one of the best of the demons, Ma1ya1-
<>dhara was killed. Rambha1 was dancing before a1ca1rya
<>Tumburu on the occasion and Puru1ravas finding fault
<>with her dance mocked at her. Rambha1 felt insulted
<>and asked the King thus: “Fool of a King, what do
<>you know of the divine dances of Devaloka?” Puru1ra-
<>vas retorted that he had learnt more of dancing from
<>Urvas4i1 than what her preceptor Tumburu knew. Tum-
<>buru got angry and cursed Puru1ravas that he would
<>live separated from Urvas4i1 till he did penance to please
<>Maha1vis2n2u. The Gandharvas then carried away
<>Urvas4i1 from Puru1ravas. (See under Puru1ravas).
<NI>5) {%Other details.%}
<NI>(i) Tumburu was a member of the court of Indra.
<>(S4loka 14, Chapter 7, Sabha1 Parva).
<NI>(ii) Tumburu was a member of the court of Kubera.
<>(S4loka 26, Chapter 10, Sabha1 Parva).
<NI>(iii) The songs of Tumburu who was a worshipper of
<>Kubera used to be heard from the mountain of Gan-
<>dhama1dana on the full-moon day. (S4loka 29, Chapter
<>159, Vana Parva).

<HI>TVAS2T2A1 I. A Praja1pati. This Praja1pati was an asura
<>also. (Su1kta 94, Anuva1ka 14, Man2d2ala 1, R2gved2a).
<NI>1) {%Birth.%} There are contradictory statements in the
<>Pura1n2as regarding the birth of Tvas2t2a1.
<NI>(a) Vis4vakarma1 got four sons named Ahirbudhnya,
<>Tvas2t2a1 Ajaikapa1t and Rudra. The great ascetic Vis4va-
<>ru1pa was the son of Tvas2t2a1. (Chapter 15, Am3s4a 1,
<>Vis2n2u Pura1n2a). [Page800-a+ 64]
<NI>(b) Kas4yapa got as his sons the Eka1das4arudras of his wife
<>Surabhi. Surabhi who became pure by penance got by
<>the grace of Maha1deva five other sons named Aja,
<>Ekapa1t, Ahirbudhnya, Tvas2t2a1 and Rudra. The noble
<>and famous Vis4varu1pa was the son of Tvas2t2a1. (Chapter
<>18, Agni Pura1n2a).
<NI>(c) Kas4yapa Mahars2i got a son named Tvas2t2a1 of his
<>wife Aditi. (S4loka 34, Chapter 226, A1di Parva).
<NI>Because of such varied statements it is not possible to
<>say whose son Tvas2t2a1 was.
<NI>2) {%Indra's enemy.%} Even from the beginning, Tvas2t2a1
<>hated Indra. Tvas2t2a1 begot of his wife Recana1 a son
<>named Vis4varu1pa to kill Indra. Vis4varu1pa was the
<>younger brother of Sannives4a. Vis4varu1pa was called
<>Tris4iras also. (See under Tris4iras). While Vis4varu1pa
<>was doing penance Indra killed him by his Vajra1yudha.
<>Enraged at this Tvas2t2a1 produced another asura named
<>Vr2tra to kill Indra. (See under Vr2tra). Indra killed
<>Vr2tra1sura also. At last greatly disappointed Tvas2t2a1
<>cursed Indra that he would suffer from Putraduh2kha
<>(loss of son) and then went to the mount Meru to do
<>penance.
<NI>3) {%Other details.%}
<NI>(i) Tvas2t2a1 also treated as a Rudra. (Chapter 15, Am3 a
<>1, Vis2n2u Pura1n2a).
<NI>(ii) When the forest of Kha1n2d2ava was burnt, he stood
<>on the side of Indra and fought against Kr2s2n2a and

<>and threw them against Arjuna and Kr2s2n2a. (S4loka 34,
<>Chapter 226, A1di Parva).
<NI>(iii) Tvas2t2a1 shines in the court of Indra. (S4loka 14,
<>Chapter 7, Sabha1 Parva).
<NI>(iv) Kus4eru, daughter of Tvas2t2a1 was once abducted
<>by Naraka1sura. (Chapter 38, Da1ks2in2a1tya Pa1t2ha, Sabha1
<>Parva).
<NI>(v) Vis4vakarma1 also used to be called Tvas2t2a1. (S4loka

<NI>(vi) The monkey called Nala was the son of Tvas2t2a1.

<>das named Cakra and Anucakra. (S4loka 40, Chapter

<HI>UCCAIS4S4RAVAS I.
<NI>1) {%Birth.%} A horse which emerged from water during
<>the churning of the sea of Milk. (See under Ks2i1ra1bdhi-
<>mathana). Devendra grabbed it the moment he saw it,
<>and thenceforth it became his vehicle. (M.B. A1di
<>Parva, Chapter 23, Verses 33-37). [Page800-b+ 65]
<NI>2) {%Colour of the horse.%} Once, during a controversy, Vinata1,
<>wife of Kas4yapa, contended that the colour of Uccais4s4ra-
<>vas was white, while another wife of Kas4yapa, Kadru1
<>said that its tail was black in colour. It was decided to bet
<>that she who got defeated in this controversy should
<>become the slave of the winner. Because the serpents,
<>the sons of Kadru1, cheated Vinata1, she had to become
<>Kadru1's slave. (See under Vinata1). (M.B. A1di Parva,
<>Chapter 20).
<NI>3) {%Laks2mi1devi1 became mare.%} Devi1 Bha1gavata relates a
<>story of Maha1laks2mi1 becoming a mare on account of
<>Uccais4 ravas. King Revanta, son of Su1rya and friend of
<>Indra, once went to Vaikun2t2ha to pay his respects to
<>Bhagava1n Vis2n2u, riding on Uccais4s4ravas. Maha1laks2mi1,
<>who was then with Vis2n2u was surprised at the arri-
<>val of Revanta. Seeing the scintillating form of
<>Uccais4s4ravas, her brother, Maha1laks2mi sat looking at
<>the horse unmindful of all other things. (Maha1laks2mi1
<>and the horse were both born from the Sea of Milk and
<>hence were sister and brother). Thus occupied Maha1-
<>laks2mi1 did not hear Maha1vis2n2u asking, “Who is this one
<>who comes like a second Cupid?” Angry at this Vis2n2u
<>said--
<NI>“So much attracted by the horse, you have not answered
<>me. Because you enjoy (Ramasi) so much your name in
<>future will be Rama1. You will also become frivolous
<>like an uncultured woman. You have never been
<>constant. Because you felt so much attracted to this
<>horse in my very presence, you will be born as a mare
<>in the world of men.”
<NI>According to this curse Maha1laks2mi1 had to be born as
<>a mare in the world; the Hehaya dynasty had its origin
<>from her. (See under Ekavi1ra). (Devi1 Bha1gavata,
<>Skandha 6).
<HI>UCCAIS4S4RAVAS II. A Maha1ra1ja of the Pu1ru dynasty.
<>He was one of the six sons of King Aviks2it. (M.B. A1di
<>Parva, Chapter 94, Verse 53).
<HI>UCCHIKHA. A serpent born in the family of Taks2aka.
<>It was burnt to death at Janamejaya's serpent yajn5a.
<>(M.B. A1di Parva, Chapter 57, Verse 9).
<HI>UCCHR2N3GA. One of the two attendants given to
<>Skanda by Vindhya. The other was named Atis4r2n3ga.
<>(M.B. S4alya Parva, Chapter 45, Verse 49).
<HI>UDA1NAVA1YU. One of the five life-breaths. The five
<>life-breaths are Pra1n2a, Apa1na, Sama1na, Uda1na and
<>Vya1na.
<HI>UDAPA1NA TI1RTHA. A holy bath on the bank of the
<>river Sarasvati1. It is said that Balabhadra Ra1ma,
<>while going on a pilgrimage, had visited this holy bath.
<>There is a story showing how this place became a
<>holy bath. Long ago there was a hermit named Gautama,
<>who had three sons called Ekata, Dvita and Trita.
<>The father was much pleased at the dutiful and devo-
<>tional character of his sons. One day he performed a
<>sacrifice and went to heaven. Then the kings and the
<>priests who were present for the sacrifice began to
<>honour and respect Trita. Ekata and Dvita did not
<>like this. The three brothers performed sacrifices and
<>acquired a large number of cows. With these cows
<>they started for the east. Trita walked before. Ekata
<>and Dvita who were behind, made a consultation and
<>drove the cows another way. Trita walked on in front,
<>alone. On the bank of the Sarasvati1 he saw a wolf and
<>getting terrified, he fell into a well in which there was
<>no water. Standing in the well, he imagined a creeper [Page801-a+ 65]
<>that was hanging to the well as ‘Soma’ (a herb used as
<>oblation in sacrifice) and performed sacrifice, chanting
<>the Vedas. His chanting was heard in heaven and
<>Br2haspati and other gods came to him and asked him
<>what boon he desired. Trita told them that he only
<>wanted to be saved from the well. Immediately the
<>river Sarasvati1 flowed into the well and the waves began
<>to swell. Standing on the waves he praised and glori-
<>fied the gods. Then he returned home and cursed
<>Ekata and Dvita and transmuted them into wolves.
<>Trita said that their children would become monkeys
<>and cattle. It happened so. The place where the Gods
<>appeared before Trita, became famous and got the name
<>Udapa1nati1rtha. (M.B. S4alya Parva, Chapter 36).
<HI>UDA1PEKS2I1. A son of Vis4va1mitra. He was a Veda1ntin.
<>(M.B. Anus4a1sana Parva, Chapter 4, Stanza 59).
<HI>UDARA1KS2A. A warrior of Skanda Deva. (M.B. S4alya
<>Parva, Chapter 45, Stanza 63).
<HI>UDARAS4A1N2D2ILYA. A hermit of the Durbar of Indra.
<>(M.B. Sabha1 Parva, Chapter 7, Stanza 31).
<HI>UDARKA. A minister of Mahis2a1sura. The ministry
<>of Mahis2a1sura was very powerful and efficient. The brave
<>and haughty Ciks2ura was the war minister. Udarka was
<>the general of the army. (See under Mahis2a1sura).
<HI>UDAYAGIRI I. The mountain of the rising. It is sup-
<>posed by poets that the Sun and the Moon rise from this
<>mountain.
<HI>UDAYAGIRI II. An ancient place of pilgrimage. It is
<>mentioned in Maha1bha1rata, Vana Parva, Chapter 84,
<>Stanza 93, that by conducting evening prayer and
<>devotion at this place once, one could obtain the fruits
<>of conducting evening prayer and meditation for twelve
<>years continuously.
<HI>UDAYANA. A renowned king of the Candravam3s4a (Lunar
<>dynasty).
<NI>1) {%Genealogy.%} Descended from Vis2n2u in the following
<>order: Brahma1-Atri-Candra-Budha-Puru1ravas-A1yus-
<>Nahus2a-Yaya1ti-Pu1ru-Janamejaya-Pra1cinva1n-Pravi1ra-
<>Namasyu-Vi1tabhaya S4un2d2u-Bahuvidha-Sam3ya1ti-Raho-
<>va1di1-Raudra1s4va-Mati1na1ra-Santurodha-Dus2yanta-
<>Bharata-Hasti-Ajami1d2ha-R2ks2a-Sam3varan2a-Kuru-Jahnu-
<>Suratha-Vid2u1ratha-Sa1rvabhauma-Jayatsena-Ravyaya-
<>Bha1vuka-Cakroddhata-Deva1tithi-R2ks2a-Bhi1ma-Prati1pa-
<>S4antanu-Vya1sa-Pa1n2d2u-Arjuna-Abhimanyu-Pari1ks2it
<>Janamejaya-S4ata1ni1ka-Sahasra1ni1ka-Udayana.
<NI>2) {%Birth.%} There was a city called Kaus4a1mbi1 situated in
<>the middle of the famous kingdom known as Vatsa in
<>North India. The palace of king S4ata1ni1ka, born of the
<>family of Arjuna, was in Kaus4a1mbi1. Vis2n2umati1 was the
<>queen of S4ata1ni1ka. She had been childless. One day
<>while S4ata1ni1ka was hunting in the forest, he met with
<>the hermit S4a1n2d2ilya, by whose blessings Vis2n2umati1 con-
<>ceived and gave birth to a son. That son was Sahas-
<>ra1ni1ka. When he came of age, S4ata1ni1ka left the country
<>with his son and went to the heaven to help the gods
<>in their battle with the Asuras, and he died there.
<>Sahasra1ni1ka became a mighty emperor. Once he got an
<>invitation from Indra to go to heaven and help the
<>gods to fight the Asuras. After having defeated the
<>Asuras, one day, he was walking with Indra in the
<>Nandana Park, when he saw the gods playing with
<>their wives in the park. Immediately the unmarried
<>king became thoughtful and Indra read correctly, the
<>reason for the sudden change in the king and said to the
<>king. “Oh King! Don't be worried. A girl becoming [Page801-b+ 65]
<>you in every aspect, is born in the world. Her name is
<>Mr2ga1vati1.”
<NI>Sahasra1ni1ka was greatly pleased at this and he returned
<>to the earth. In the chariot there were Tilottama1 and
<>the charioteer, with the king. The king who was deeply
<>immersed in thinking about Mr2ga1vati1, did not attend
<>to the conversation of Tilottama1, who getting angry
<>cursed him thus:-“May you be separated for fourteen
<>years from the person whose thought has prevented
<>you from attending to what I have been telling you.”
<NI>The king married Mr2ga1vati1. She became pregnant.
<>One day she told the king about her desire to dip in a
<>pond of blood. The king got a pond ready, filled with
<>the juice of La1ks2a1 (a kind of wax, the boiled water of
<>which will look like blood) and such other things. Mr2ga1-
<>vati1 began to dip and splash in the pond of blood.
<>When she was dipping under the juice, taking her to be
<>a large piece of flesh, an eagle took her from the pond
<>and flew away. The king was overwhelmed with grief
<>and fell down. Then the charioteer came down from
<>heaven and informed the king of the curse of Tilottama1,
<>and then he returned.
<NI>The eagle left Mr2ga1vati1 in the mount of the Rising Sun
<>and flew away. She cried aloud. A huge snake neared
<>her to swallow her. Then a divine person appeared
<>there and saved her from the snake and vanished. Then
<>a hermit-boy came there and asked the lonely woman,
<>clad in only one garment, about her story and took her
<>to the hermitage of the hermit Jamadagni who blessed
<>her. After some days she gave birth to a son. At that
<>time an unknown voice was heard saying “This boy
<>would become the most renowned king Udayana and
<>his son would become the supreme Lord of the Vidya1-
<>dharas.” Because he was born in the Udaya1dri (the
<>mount of the Rising Sun) he got the name Udayana.
<>The boy Udayana grew up in the hermitage.
<NI>3) {%Udayana to his father.%} The hermit Jamadagani who
<>knew the past, present and the future performed all the
<>rituals, necessary for a boy of Ks2atriya caste (kingly
<>race) such as Caula, Upanayana etc. and gave him
<>education in every branch of knowledge. Because of her
<>love and regard for her son, Mr2ga1vati1 put on his arm a
<>bangle with the name Sahasra1ni1ka inscribed in it,
<>which she had been wearing so long. One day, while
<>Udayana was walking through the forest, he saw a
<>snake-charmer catching a snake. He felt sorry for the
<>snake. So he gave the bangle to the snake-charmer and
<>set the snake free. When the snake charmer was gone,
<>the snake told Udayana its story. That serpent was
<>Vasunemi, the elder brother of Va1suki. Out of grati-
<>tude the serpent gave Udayana the famous Lute
<>Ghos2avati1 and betels and taught him the art of making
<>garlands and marks on the forehead which would never
<>fade.
<NI>The snake-charmer took the bangle to the capital for sale.
<>Seeing the name of the king inscribed on it, the king's
<>men took him before the king. He told the king every-
<>thing. The king who had been suffering for the last four-
<>teen years form the pangs of separation, started for the
<>mount of the Rising Sun, without any loss of time. The
<>hermit Jamadagni gave him his wife Mr2ga1vati1 and son
<>Udayana. They all returned to Kaus4a1mbi1.
<NI>4) {%The anointment of Udayana.%} Sahasra1ni1ka anointed his
<>son Udayana as the heir to his throne, and appointed
<>Yaugandhara1yan2a, Rumanva1n and Vasantaka, the sons [Page802-a+ 65]
<>of three ministers, as ministers of Udayana. At the time
<>of the anointment there was a shower of flowers
<>from the sky and an unknown voice said “With the help
<>of these ministers Udayana would bring the whole of
<>the earth under his control.” After a time Sahasra1ni1ka
<>went to the Hima1layas with his wife for penance.
<NI>5). {%Va1savadatta1 became Udayana's wife.%} A daughter was
<>born to the king of Ujjayini1. Her name was Va1sava-
<>datta1. Her father Can2d2amaha1sena decided to give her
<>in marriage to Udayana the king of Vatsa. How to
<>bring this to pass? Can2d2amaha1sena and Udayana had
<>been enemies. Finally he found out a way. It was
<>to entrust Va1savadatta1 to Udayana (who was a great
<>teacher of music) for teaching her music. Ultimately he
<>would fall in love with her and thus Udayana would
<>become his son-in-law. This was the plan.
<NI>King Can2d2amaha1sena sent a messenger to Kaus4a1mbi1.
<>The messenger was sent back with a reply that, if his
<>daughter was sent to Kaus4a1mbi1, he would teach her
<>music. Can2d2amaha1sena did not like this. So he decided
<>to take Udayana a prisoner somehow or other. The
<>king had an elephant called Nad2a1giri. He ordered for
<>an artificial elephant to be made equal in size to
<>Nad2a1giri, and placed some soldiers inside the elephant.
<>The artificial elephant with soldiers inside it was taken
<>to the great forest in the Vindhya mountain and placed
<>there. The men of Udayana saw this elephant and
<>reported it to the king. Udayana decided to see the huge
<>elephant which had appeared in the Vindhya. Udayana
<>went to the forest and saw the huge elephant standing
<>at a distance. The king found out a plan to catch it.
<>Playing mild notes on his lute, the king alone neared
<>the elephant. As the night was drawing and as
<>he was immersed in music, he did not understand that
<>it was an artificial elephant. As the king was nearing
<>the elephant it went on retreating, and thus got the
<>king away from his men. Then the soldiers got out of
<>the elephant, surrounded the king and took him a
<>prisoner. Thus Udayana began to live in the palace of
<>Can2d2amaha1sena. His work was to teach Va1savadatta1
<>music.
<NI>The news reached Kaus4a1mbi1. Yaugandhara1yan2a entrust-
<>ed the affairs of the government to Ruman2va1n and
<>started for Ujjayini1 with Vasantaka. At Ujjayini1 they
<>got Yoges4vara, a Brahmara1ks2asa as friend. According
<>to his advice Yaugandhara1yan2a took the guise of a
<>mad old man. Vasantaka adopted the guise of a sick
<>man, suffering from pain in the stomach an uncouth
<>figure to look at. They entered the city. The madness of
<>Yaugandhara1yan2a was an entertainment to the people.
<>The ladies of the court liked him much. Va1savadatta1
<>invited the madman to the harem. Udayana instantly
<>recognized the mad man. Vasantaka also got admittance
<>to the palace. He told Va1savadatta1 the story of Loha-
<>jan3gha in an interesting way. (See under Lohajan3gha)
<>Va1savadatta1 began to be drawn more and more towards
<>Udayana. She seemed to have forgotten even about the
<>fact that her father was an enemy of Udayana, who
<>had been thinking seriously of means of escape from
<>the palace. Va1savadatta1 agreed to accompany him.
<>A1s2a1dhaka got Bhadra1vati1, the elephant of Va1savadatta1,
<>ready for the flight. In the night Udayana and his
<>retinue got on the elephant Bhadra1vati1 and fled from
<>the palace. Ka1n5canama1la1 the maid of Va1savadatta1
<>also accompanied her mistress. When they had passed [Page802-b+ 64]
<>the Vindhya mountain the elephant Bhadra1vati1 fell
<>dead. When they all were standing around the dead
<>elephant sadly, they heard an ethereal voice saying, “Oh
<>King! I am a Vidya1dhara woman called Ma1ya1vati1. I
<>had been an elephant for so long. The son you are
<>going to get, will also be helped by me. Your wife
<>Va1savadatta1 also, is a goddess, born as a woman
<>purposely.” Next day, all reached the palace of Udayana
<>and the marriage of Udayana and Va1savadatta1 took
<>place shortly. Can2d2amaha1sena recognized that marri-
<>age.
<NI>6) {%Udayana's marriage with Padma1vati1.%} Udayana spent
<>his days with Va1savadatta1 in the harem. The ministers
<>Yaugandhara1yan2a, Ruman2va1n, Vasantaka and others
<>thought that the behaviour of the King was detrimental
<>to the well-being of the country. They wanted to re-
<>move the King from the palace for a little while and
<>to form an alliance with the powerful King of Magadha.
<>By a marriage alliance all these could be achieved. The
<>King of Magadha had a beautiful daughter called
<>Padma1vati1. The ministers began to work with this end
<>in view.
<NI>Once Yaugandhara1yan2a took Udayana to the forest of
<>La1va1n2aka and stayed there. It was reported to the
<>King of Magadha that the King of Vatsa was drawing
<>near to his kingdom. Fearing an attack from Udayana,
<>the King of Magadha began to think of concluding a
<>treaty with Vatsa. The King of Vatsa used to go for
<>hunting everyday. One day he went to a distant place
<>for hunting, and the minister went to the house of
<>Va1savadatta1 and informed her of their plans. Though
<>it was not at all palatable to her, she gave her consent
<>and agreed to help them as it was meant for the well-
<>being of the King and the country. Accordingly,
<>Yaugandhara1yan2a took the guise of an old Brahmin,
<>Va1savadatta1 that of a young Brahmin lady and Vasan-
<>taka that of a Brahmin celibate with only one eye.
<>They went to the kingdom of Magadha. Ruman2va1n
<>set fire to the house of Va1savadatta1 and spread the
<>rumour that Va1savadatta1 and Vasantaka had been
<>burnt to death. Yaugandhara1yan2a, Va1savadatta1 and
<>Vasantaka reached Magadha. They got into the capital
<>and saw Padma1vati1 sitting in the garden. The old
<>Brahmin conversed with the princess for a while. She
<>enquired about the young woman who was with him.
<>The old Brahmin replied thus:--“She is my daughter
<>Avantika1. Her husband has left the country. I request
<>you to keep her with you till I find him out and bring
<>him here. She may not like to be separated from her
<>people. So let her brother, the celibate, also be here
<>with her.”
<NI>Padma1vati1 took them with gladness and Yaugandhara1-
<>yan2a, bidding farewell, returned to the forest La1va1n2aka.
<>Avantika1 and the Celibate lived in the palace with
<>Padma1vati1. Va1savadatta1 who had learned from Udayana
<>the art of making garlands ans marks on the forehead
<>which would not fade, had prepared them for Padma1-
<>vati1.
<NI>The King of Vatsa returned to the forest La1va1n2aka
<>and found the house of his wife burnt down to ashes.
<>He fell unconscious when he heard that Va1savadatta1
<>and Vasantaka had been burnt to death.
<NI>The spies of the King of Magadha who were in the
<>forest of La1va1n2aka, reported the rumour about the [Page803-a+ 64]
<>death of Va1savadatta1 and Vasantaka to their King in
<>Magadha, who wished to give his daughter Padma1vati1
<>in marriage to Udayana. The marriage proposal was
<>accepted by Udayana and wearing garlands and marks
<>that would not fade Padma1vati1 entered the wedding
<>dais. Udayana married Padma1vati1. Yaugandhara1yan2a
<>made the King of Magadha take an oath that he would
<>go for no more aggression. Udayana and his people
<>reached Kaus4a1mbi1. On the way the King happened to
<>see the mark on the forehead and the garland on the
<>neck of Padma1vati1 and asked her who had made them.
<>Padma1vati1 told the King the story of Avantika1.
<>Udayana was definite that Avantika1 was Va1savadatta1
<>herself. Avantika1 was brought before the King. Padma1-
<>vati1 congratulated Va1savadatta1. Both of them loved
<>each other and lived together as the loving wives of
<>Udayana. (Katha1saritsa1gara, La1va1n2akalambaka).
<NI>7) {%Udayana gets a new throne.%} Once Udayana was
<>sitting in the court-hall, when a Brahmin came there
<>and made a complaint to the King that some cow-
<>herds had broken the legs of his son. The Brahmin
<>said that a boy named Devasena sat on a stone in the
<>forest and instantly he got kingly power. The leg of the
<>Brahmin boy was broken by the friends of Devasena
<>because he did not bow before Devasena.
<NI>When he heard the story, the minister Yaugandhara1-
<>yan2a said that that place must have some peculiarities.
<>Accordingly the men of the King dug the place. He
<>got a throne of gems. (Katha1saritsa1gara, La1va1n2akalam-
<>baka).
<NI>8) {%The son of Udayana.%} Va1savadatta1 became pregnant
<>and gave birth to a child. He was named Narava1hana-
<>datta. Na1rada granted him a boon that Narava1hana-
<>datta would become the emperor of the Vidya1dharas.
<>(See under Narava1hanadatta).
<NI>The princess of Taks2as4ila1 named Kalin3gasena1 fell in
<>love with Udayana and she came to Kaus4a1mbi1. But no
<>marriage took place. (See under Kalin3gasena1). Nara-
<>va1hanadatta, the son of Udayana, married Madana-
<>man5cuka1 who was the incarnation of Rati Devi1 (the
<>wife of Madana). Udayana entrusted the country
<>to his son and led a life of retirement with his wives.
<>(Katha1saritsa1gara).
<HI>UDDA1LAKA I. A disciple called A1run2i of the teacher
<>A1yodhadhaumya. To know how A1run2i got the name
<>Udda1laka, see under A1yodhadhaumya.
<NI>It is stated in Maha1bha1rata, Sabha1 Parva, Chapter 7,
<>Stanza 12 that this hermit Udda1laka was a prominent
<>figure in the Durbar of Indra. Udda1laka had a son cal-
<>led S4vetaketu and a daughter called Suja1ta1. He gave
<>his daughter Suja1ta1 in marriage to his favourite disci-
<>ple Kahod2aka. The hermit As2t2a1vakra was their son. See
<>under As2t2a1vakra. (M.B. Vana Parva, Chapter 132).
<>Once Udda1laka caused the river Sarasvati1 to appear at
<>the place of sacrifice. From that day onwards Sarasvati1
<>got the name ‘Manorama1’ because when the thought
<>came to his mind (manas) the river made its appearance.
<>(M.B. S4alya Parva, Chapter 33). It is mentioned in
<>Maha1bha1rata, S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 57, Stanza 10, that
<>Udda1laka expelled his son S4vetaketu from the house be-
<>cause the son was a hater of Brahmins.
<HI>UDDA1LAKA II. The story of another hermit of the name
<>Udda1laka is mentioned in the Maha1bha1rata, Anus4a1sana
<>Parva. Chapter 71. This hermit is known as Udda1laki [Page803-b+ 65]
<>also. Once this hermit happened to forget that he had
<>left flowers, food and his waterpot on the bank of the
<>river and reaching his hermitage, he asked his son
<>Na1ciketa to fetch them from the bank of the river.
<>When Na1ciketa reached the bank of the river, those
<>things had been washed down by the current. The son
<>returned and reported the matter to his father. The
<>father got angry and cursed his son to death. Seeing
<>the son lying dead on darbha (mattress made of darbha
<>grass) the hermit cried aloud. In that flow of tears life
<>returned to the body and the son woke up as if from
<>sleep. The father asked the son about the news of the
<>realm of Yama (the god of death) and the son told the
<>hermit the news about the world of the dead.
<HI>UDDAN2D2AS4A1STRI1. One of the eighteen and a half
<>famous poets of Kerala. He was a Sanskrit poet. His
<>native place was La1t2apura on the bank of river Pa1la1r
<>in Ton2d2aman2d2ala in the Tamilnad. The name of his
<>father was S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a and that of his mothter was Ran3ga1-
<>devi1. Poet Ulloor says that S4a1stri1 had another name
<>Irugupana1tha. He had a very good education. After
<>having completed his education, he travelled through
<>A1ndhra, Karn2a1t2aka, Kalin3ga, Cola, Kerala and many
<>other countries and finally came to Kozhikode and
<>visited the King Ma1navikramamaha1ra1ja. At the instance
<>of the king he composed the drama called Mallika1ma1-
<>rutam. Besides this we have obtained only the ‘Kokila-
<>sandes4a’ and some other single poems of S4a1stri1. It is said
<>that there is a thesis on dramas also. S4a1stri1 was not
<>in the habit of respecting those who did not pay respect
<>to him, however superior they might be. So some say
<>that he was arrogant. A Malaya1la Brahmin called
<>Bhat2t2atiri of Ka1kkas4s4eri, rose against S4a1stri1 in Kerala.
<HI>UDDHAVA.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} A Ya1dava. He was a friend and
<>minister of S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a. In Maha1bha1rata, A1di Parva,
<>Chapter 186, Stanza 18, mention is made that Uddhava
<>was present on the occasion of the Svayam3vara (marriage)
<>of Draupadi1. It is mentioned in Maha1bha1rata, A1di
<>Parva, Chapter 218, Stanza 11, that at a famous cele-
<>bration held in the mountain of Raivata, Uddhava was
<>present. (See under Subhadra1).
<NI>Uddhava was a disciple of Br2haspati, and a man of
<>great intelligence. It was this Uddhava who brought the
<>dowry of Subhadra1 to Indraprastha, when Arjuna
<>married her. (M.B. A1di Parva, Chapter 220, Stanza
<>30).
<NI>Once a king named S4a1lva besieged the city of Dva1r-
<>aka1. At that time Uddhava saved Dva1raka1. (M.B.
<>Vana Parva, Chapter 15, Stanza 9).
<NI>2). {%The message carried by Uddhava.%} Kam3sa sent Akru1ra
<>to Amba1d2i, and brought S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a to Mathura1. S4ri1
<>Kr2s2n2a killed Kam3sa and made Ugrasena king, and

<>to end. Uddhava felt grief and requested S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a

<>S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a taught Uddhava the doctrine that the body
<>of man and such other things seen in the whole universe

<HI>UGRASENA I. King Ugrasena, father of Kam3sa.
<NI>1) {%Genealogy.%} Descended from Vis2n2u thus: Brahma1-
<>Atri-Candra-Budha-Puru1ravas-A1yus-Nahus2a-Yaya1ti-
<>Yadu-Sahasrajit-S4atajit-Hehaya-Dharma-Kunti-(Kun2i)-
<>Bhadrasena-Dhanaka-Kr2tavi1rya-Ka1rttavi1rya1rjuna-
<>Madhu-Vr2s2n2i-Yudha1jit-S4ini-Satyaka-Sa1tyaki (Yuyu-
<>dha1na)-Yaya-Kun2i-Anamitra-Pr2s4ni-Citraratha-Kuku1ra
<>Vahni-Viloma1-Kapotaloma1-Tumburu-Dundubhi-
<>Daridra-Vasu-Na1huka-A1huka-Ugrasena-Kam3sa.
<NI>2) {%Ugrasena became king.%} Ugrasena became king of Mathu-
<>ra1puri1. His Kingship was not a hereditary acquisition.
<>There is a story behind it. In olden days, in the plateau
<>of Ka1lindi1 there was a famous place called Madhuvana.
<>The place was called so because it was the abode of an
<>Asura named Madhu. Madhu had a son, Lavan2a. S4atru-
<>ghna killed him as he was a very troublesome fellow
<>and a thorn on the side of the Devas. S4atrughna then
<>established a beautiful kingdom there and ruled it. He
<>named it Mathura1. After the death of S4atrughna his
<>two sons ruled Mathura1. Then, when the Solar dynasty
<>came to its end, Mathura1 came under the Ya1davas.
<>A Ya1dava king called S4u1rasena ruled over the kingdom.
<>Vasudeva, father of S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a was the son of S4u1rasena.
<>After the death of his father Vasudeva took up the pro-
<>fession of herding cows, and therefore Ugrasena,
<>another king of the Ya1dava dynasty had to become king
<>of Mathura1. (Devi1 Bha1gavata, 4th Skandha).
<NI>3) {%Ugrasena and Kam3sa.%} There is a common belief that
<>Kam3sa was the son of Ugrasena. But, the Bha1gavata
<>relates the following to the effect that Kam3sa was born
<>to a Gandharva called Dramila of Ugrasena's wife.
<NI>When once Ugrasena's wife was in her monthly periods,
<>she walked in the forest with her companions. A Gan-
<>dharva called Dramila saw her then, felt attracted by her
<>and made her pregnant. Angered at this, she cursed
<>Dramila thus: “Since you have procreated a son in me,
<>while I am in my periods this son will be killed by a
<>boy born in my husband's family.” Kam3sa was the son
<>born to her in the above manner. Kam3sa ascended the
<>throne after putting Ugrasena in prison. According to the
<>curse of Ugrasena's wife, S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a was born in Ugra-
<>sena's family and he killed Kam3sa. Na1rada had informed
<>Kam3sa of the Dramila interlude. Kam3sa told this story
<>secretly to Akru1ra when the latter was deputed by him
<>to invite Kr2s2n2a to the dhanur yajn5a. (Bha1gavata, 10th
<>Skandha).
<NI>{%The name A1huka.%} Genealogy states that Ugrasena was
<>the son of A1huka. But, in certain contexts Ugrasena
<>is called A1huka also. “Afterwards we made A1huka-
<>Ugrasena King...” (M.B. Udyoga Parva, Chapter
<>128, Verse 39). [Page805-a+ 64]
<NI>5) {%Ugrasena imprisoned.%} Vasudeva, father of S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a
<>was Ugrasena's minister. Kam3sa, when he attained
<>majority imprisoned Ugrasena and became himself king.
<>(M.B. Sabha1 Parva, Chapter 22).
<NI>6) {%Ugrasena regained kingdom.%} S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a killed Kam3sa with
<>the permission of Ugrasena and made him king again.
<>During the reign of Ugrasena, Jara1sandha and S4a1lva
<>attacked Mathura1puri1. (See under Kr2s2n2a).
<NI>7) {%Ugrasena and the iron rod.%} While Ugrasena was ruling
<>the Kingdom, the sages Vis4va1mitra, Na1rada and Kan5ja
<>once came to Dva1raka1. To insult the sages, the Ya1davas
<>brought before them, Sa1mba dressed as a pregnant
<>woman. The Ya1davas told the sages that she was Babhru's
<>wife, and wanted to be told whether the child she deli-
<>vered would be male or female. The sages understood
<>their evil mentality, and prophesied that Sa1mba would
<>deliver an iron rod fierce enough to annihilate the
<>whole Ya1dava race. According to the prophecy the
<>next day Sa1mba delivered an iron rod. The Ya1davas
<>imparted the news to Ugrasena, who got the iron rod
<>reduced to powder and deposited the powder in the sea.
<>He also enforced prohibition of liquor in the country.
<>(To know how the powder of the rod ruined the Ya1dava
<>dynasty see under Kr2s2n2a). (M.B. Mausala Parva,
<>Chapter 1).
<NI>8) {%After death.%} After his death, Ugrasena joined the
<>Vis4vadevata1s. Bhu1ris4ravas, S4ala, Bhu1ri, Kam3sa-
<>Ugrasena, Vasudeva, Uttara with his brother S4an3kha-
<>these kings (after death) joined the company of Vis4va-
<>devata1s. (M.B. Svarga1rohan2a Parva, Chapter 5, Verses
<>16, 17).

<HI>ULU1PI1. Wife of Arjuna.
<NI>1) {%How she became the wife of Arjuna.%} Once Arjuna
<>happened to enter the palace in which Dharmaputra
<>was living with Pa1n5ca1li1. As a result, Arjuna had to go
<>on a pilgrimage for a year. (See under Ira1va1n). Arjuna
<>reached Gan3ga1dva1ra. When he got down into the river
<>Gan3ga1, he saw Ulu1pi1 the daughter of Na1gara1ja (King
<>of the serpents). He asked her a few questions. She
<>told him thus:--“I am the daughter of the serpent
<>Kauravya of the family of Aira1vata. I came to bathe
<>in the river and when I saw you I grew amorous.”
<>Arjuna told her that Dharmaputra had imposed on him
<>celibacy for twelve months and that it was not
<>right to marry in the meantime. Ulu1pi1 argued with
<>Arjuna and convinced him that it was not wrong to
<>marry her. Arjuna married her. A son named Ira1va1n
<>was born to her.
<NI>2) {%How Ulu1pi1 caused Arjuna to be killed and how he was
<>brought to life again.%} (See paras 28 and 29 under
<>Arjuna).
<NI>3) {%The end of Ulu1pi1.%} After having brought Arjuna back
<>to life, Ulu1pi1 reached Hastina1pura with Babhruva1hana
<>and Citra1n3gada1. (M.B. As4vamedha Parva, Chapter
<>87). As soon as she reached there she greeted Kunti1,
<>Draupadi1 and Subhadra1. She gave them various kinds
<>of presents. It is mentioned in Maha1bha1rata, As4rama-
<>va1sika Parva, Chapter I, Stanza 23 that Ulu1pi1 served
<>Ga1ndha1ri1 at one time. In Maha1bha1rata, A1s4ramava1sika
<>Parva, Chapter 10, Stanza 46 it is mentioned that Ulu1pi1
<>was greatly loved by the subjects. When the Pa1n2d2avas
<>began the ‘great departure’ (Maha1prastha1na) Ulu1pi1
<>entered the River Ganges. Citra1n3gada1 went to Man2alu1-
<>rapura.
<NI>“Ulu1pi1, the daughter of the serpent Kauravya, jumped
<>into the Ganges and to Man2alu1rapura, went Citra1n3-
<>gada1.” (Bha1s2a1 Bha1rata, Maha1prastha1nika Parva, Chap-
<>ter 1, Stanza 27).
<NI>4) {%The other names of Ulu1pi1.%} Bhujaga1tmaja1, Bhujagendra-

<HI>UN5CHAVR2TTI. A brahmin. His story is told as follows
<>in Jaimini As4vamedha Parva.
<NI>This poor brahmin who lived by begging got one day
<>some food grain powder. After offering a portion of it
<>to Agni and Brahmins, he divided the balance equally
<>between the children. Then he sat down to take his own
<>food when Dharmadeva, disguised as a brahmin,
<>appeared and demanded food. Un5chavr2tti gave all his
<>food to the guest. Since that did not satisfy the guest,
<>the sons also gave their shares of the food to him. Great-
<>ly pleased at the noble act of Un5chavr2tti, Dharmadeva
<>took the brahmin family with him to Svargaloka. One
<>day a few particles of the foodgrain powder which re-
<>mained with the brahmin fell on the earth. A mongoose
<>came and played on that ground. That part of his body
<>which got smeared with the food-grain powder became
<>golden in colour. Though the mongoose went to the
<>yajn5a ground of Dharmadeva and repeated the above
<>process there, the remaining portion of its body did not
<>become golden.
<HI>UN2D2RA (M) (UT2RAM). A place in South India.

<HI>UNMADA1. A celestial woman.
<NI>1) {%Became a woman by the curse of Uravas4i1.%} Ham3sa, the
<>King of Gandharvas (semi-gods) had a general of the
<>army called Durmada. He was a dangler. He had an
<>eye on Urvas4i1. She was the wife of Puru1ravas a famous
<>King. On several occasions Durmada followed Urvas4i1,
<>with lustful desire. He had expressed his amour for her
<>on several occasions. But Urvas4i1 did not pay any heed
<>to his words.
<NI>One day Puru1ravas and Urvas4i1 were present in the
<>durbar of Indra. Puru1ravas and Urvas4i1 had signalled
<>a rendezvous for that night at the corner of the Nan-
<>dana Park. Durmada understood this. He called a
<>celestial woman named Unmada1 to his side. They made
<>a plan and accordingly Unmada1 disguised herself as
<>Urvas4i1 and Durmada took the guise of Puru1ravas and
<>both of them entered Nandana park. Puru1ravas went to
<>Unmada1 and conjugated with her. In the same way
<>Urvas4i1 received Durmada, mistaking him for Puru1ravas.
<>After the conjugation Durmada laughed loud as if he
<>had played a trick on Urvas4i1. Urvas4i1 understood every-
<>thing. Puru1ravas also arrived there. Urvas4i1 cursed
<>Durmada to take birth in the earth as a Ra1ks2asa and
<>cursed Unmada1 to be born in the earth as the daughter
<>of a King and she said that at that time she would love
<>one man and become the wife of another man. The
<>aggrieved Durmada and Unmada1 prayed for liberation
<>from the curse. Urvas4i1 gave them liberation thus:--
<>“This Durmada will be born as the son of Unmada1.
<>Seeing the death of her husband and son, she would
<>jump into fire. After that she will enter heaven.
<>Durmada will be killed by the sword of an enemy and
<>will obtain heaven.” According to this curse Durmada
<>was born as the son of Di1rghajan3gha, the emperor of
<>Hiran2yapura, under the name Pinga1ks2a and Unmada1 [Page807-a+ 65]
<>was born as the daughter of the King of Videha. Her
<>name was Harin2i1 (Brahma1n2d2a Pura1n2a, Chapter 3).
<NI>2) {%The marriage and death of Harin2i1.%} Harin2i1 grew up to
<>be a young woman Once Pin3ga1ks2a growing lustful took
<>Harin2i1 and went through the sky. She cried aloud for

<>the marriage was fixed. Invitations were sent to many
<>Kings. Among them there was a king named Bhadra-
<>s4ren2ya, who took her by force and went away. There
<>was a fierce battle between the two Kings, Bhadra-
<>s4ren2ya and Vasumanas and Vasumanas was defeated. See-
<>ing this Divoda1sa, the King of Ka1s4i1, attacked Bhadras4re-
<>n2ya. Though Divoda1sa defeated Bhadras4ren2ya, he did

<NI>When all this news reached Vasumanas, the King
<>of Ayodhya1, he became jealous of Bhadras4ren2ya. A

<HI>UPANIS2AD. The four Vedas are R2k, Yajus, Sa1ma and
<>Atharva. Each of these four has a Bra1hman2a (a treatise
<>relating to prayer and sacrificial ceremony).
<>Next come the A1ran2yakas (forest texts--writings meant
<>for the forest-dwelling hermit) as appendices to the
<>Bra1hman2as. Then come the Upanis2ads as appendices
<>to the A1ran2yakas. These four classes of literary works
<>(the Vedas, the Bra1hman2as, the A1ran2yakas and the
<>Upanis2ads) constitute the Vedic literature proper. The
<>A1ran2yakas and the Upanis2ads are inseparably connected
<>with each other. The Upanis2ads are called Veda1ntas
<>(the end of the Vedas). The bulk of these Veda1ntas
<>belong to different periods anterior to the Later Vedic
<>Period. The students begin the study of Upanis2ads
<>only after having completed the study of the Mantras
<>(Vedic hymns) and the Bra1hman2as (the ritual). [Page808-b+ 64]
<NI>The meaning of the word ‘Upanis2ad’ is that which is
<>most near. Upa = near. ni = most. sad = exist.
<>(or sit). The Upanis2ads can be called the Jn5a1naka1n2d2a
<>of the Vedas. They describe the nature of Brahman.
<>The figure of the supreme Spirit (Brahman) exists in
<>the Upanis2ads. Apparently the Upanis2ads are expla-
<>nations of the mantras, but they are concerned more
<>with the allegorical significations and the mystic mean-
<>ings of the tattvas or essence, of the origin of life, the
<>world, the soul, God etc. The Upanis2ads are the basis
<>of the S2ad2-dars4anas, the six systems of philosophy.
<>There are a large number of Upanis2ads. The most
<>important among them are 108 in number.
<HI>UPAPA1TAKA (UPAPA1PA) (Minor sins). In accord-
<>ance with the Ra1s2trami1ma1m3sa1 (political philosophy)
<>of Ancient India, crimes were divided into two types.
<>They were called Upapa1takas (minor crimes) and
<>Pa1takas (major crimes). To know about major crimes
<>(Pa1takas) see under Pa1pa (sin). Upapa1takas are given
<>below:--Cow-slaughter; sacrificing by one who is
<>unworthy to perform it; seducing another man's wife;
<>forsaking one's father, mother and teacher; forsaking
<>self-study, agni (fire) and son; becoming Parivetta1 (one
<>who gets married before one's elder brother is married.)
<>Younger brother finishing education before the elder;
<>giving an unmarried girl to Parivitti or Parivetta1;
<>performing sacrifice by a parivitti or a parivetta1; slan-
<>dering an unmarried girl; Living on the interest of
<>money that is lent; violating one's vow; selling pond,
<>garden, wife or son; becoming an outcaste; forsaking
<>relatives; Teaching the Vedas after receiving remune-
<>ration; selling things which should not be sold; working
<>in mines; working with big machinery; destroying
<>medicinal herbs; living by women; to impede rites;
<>cut down fresh trees (not dried) for fire-wood; kidnap-
<>ping women; mingling with slanderers of women;
<>selfish activities; eating forbidden rice; not keeping
<>Sacrificial fire; theft; not repaying loan; learning for-
<>bidden sciences; doing things which are bad and will
<>cause grief to others; stealing of base metals, grains and
<>cows; contact with drunken women; killing women,
<>S4u1dra, Vais4ya and Ks2atriya and becoming an infidel
<>are all Upapa1takas.
<NI>Causing grief to a Brahmin; inhaling the smell of liquor
<>and other prohibited things; resorting to tricks or
<>deceit and engaging in pederasty are sins which would
<>make one an outcaste.
<NI>Slaughter of dog, donkey, camel, lion, sheep, jungle-
<>goat, fish, serpent and mungoose are sins of a mixed
<>character.
<NI>Receiving money from the despicable; buying and
<>selling; serving a s4u1dra; telling a lie; acting so as to
<>render oneself unworthy; killing worms and birds;
<>eating food along with liquor; stealing fruits, flowers
<>and butea; and becoming a coward are also sins.
