<HI>VIKRAMA1DITYA. Vikrama1ditya, who is believed to be
<>one of the mighty emperors of Bha1rata, was an extra-
<>ordinarily wise, righteous and valiant ruler. There are
<>several stories in all the languages of India, prevalent every-
<>where. They are generally called Vikrama1ditya stories.
<>Vikrama1ditya was the son of Mahendra1ditya, King of
<>Ujjayini1. Mahendra1ditya and his wife Saumyadars4ana1
<>were in great distress as they were childless. Sumati,
<>the Prime Minister, Vajra1yudha, the army commander,
<>and Mahi1dhara, the priest, were as distressed as the
<>royal couple. The King and the queen engaged them-
<>selves in fast and prayer.
<NI>In the meanwhile, the Devas found life extremely
<>difficult due to the wicked deeds of the barbarians, and
<>they went to Kaila1sa and told Rudradeva of their
<>grievances. They said, “Oh! Lord! All the asuras
<>exterminated by yourself and Maha1vis2n2u, are born
<>on the earth as Barbarians. They commit great sins
<>such as killing the Brahmins, obstructing sacrifices
<>carrying away hermit damsels etc. The sacrificial
<>offerings in the sacred fire with Vedic Mantras by
<>Brahmins, is the food of Devas. Because of the troubles
<>caused by the Barbarians in the earth, the sacrifices are
<>hindered and the Devas are in trouble due to lack of
<>food. So a being, mighty and strong enough to ex-
<>terminate all the Barbarians on the earth, should take
<>incarnation.”
<NI>S4iva agreed and sent the devas back to their world.
<>Then he called Ma1lyava1n and told him to take birth
<>as the son of Mahendra1ditya in the city of Ujjayini1. [Page855-a+ 64]
<>S4iva added. “You should exterminate all the Barbarians
<>and reinstate rituals and ceremonies. The Yaks2as,
<>Ra1ks2asas, ghosts etc. will be under your control. You
<>will be an emperor there with divine powers.” Accord-
<>ingly Ma1lyava1n took birth as the son of Mahendra1-
<>ditya. That infant was Vikrama1ditya who became a
<>mighty emperor later. (Katha1saritsa1gara, Vis2amas4i1la-
<>lambaka, Taran3ga 1).
<HI>VIKRAMAS4I1LA. A King praised in the Ma1rkan2d2eya

<HI>VIKUKS2I. A son of Iks2va1ku. It is said that Iks2va1ku
<>was born from the spittle of Manu. It is stated in Devi1
<>Bha1gavata, Skandha 7, that after the death of S4arya1ti,
<>the Ra1ks2asas (giants) attacked Ayodhya1 and the sons
<>of the King having fled to different directions, Iks2va1ku
<>continued the dynasty of S4arya1ti in Ayodhya1. Hundred
<>sons beginning with Vikuks2i, were born to Iks2va1ku.
<>Of these hundred sons fifty were employed to rule
<>over the regions of East and North and fortyeight, to
<>rule over the regions in the south and the west. With
<>the remaining two sons the King stayed in Ayodhya1,
<>and carried on administration.
<NI>One day King Iks2va1ku resolved to conduct the great
<>sacrifice of offering to the manes called Maha1pralaya-
<>s4ra1ddha, for which preparations were speedily made.
<>The hermits such as Vasis2t2ha and others arrived
<>according to invitation. He sent his son Vikuks2i to the
<>forest to bring the required amount of flesh for the
<>sacrifice. Vikuks2i entered the forest and hunted hare,
<>hog, deer etc. and collected the required quantity of
<>flesh; but on the way home, he became tired of hunger.
<>To appease his hunger he took a small hare from the
<>collection cooked it and ate it. He took the balance to
<>the King who was much pleased with his son and gave
<>the animals to Vasis2t2ha the family priest for proks2an2a
<>(sprinkling of holy water on the animals before sacri-
<>fice). But Vasis2t2ha got angry and said, “flesh which
<>constitutes remains is not acceptable.” The king
<>understood the truth only then. He was filled with
<>anger and distress. He expelled Vikuks2i from his
<>country for this misdeed. Thus because he had eaten
<>a S4as4a (hare) Vikuks2i got another name S4as4a1da.
<>S4as4a1da not at all caring about the misfortune that be-
<>fell him, went to the forest and lived on fruits and
<>roots and worshipped Devi1, with ardent devotion.
<NI>Iks2va1ku died. S4as4a1da knew this and returned to
<>Ayodhya1 and assumed reign. He performed several [Page855-b+ 63]
<>sacrifices on the banks of river Sarayu1. The famous
<>Kakutstha was the son of this Vikuks2i. (Devi1
<>Bha1gavata, Skandha 7).
<HI>VIKUN2D2ALA. A Vais4ya who obtained heaven by
<>bathing during the month Ma1gha in the waters of
<>Ka1lindi1. This Vais4ya was a deplorable sinner. Still the
<>men of Ka1la (Yama) sent Vikun2d2ala to heaven without
<>minding his sins. This story occurs in Padma Pura1n2a,
<>A1di Khan2d2a, Chapter 30, as follows:
<NI>In days of old there lived a Vais4ya named Hema-
<>kun2d2ala in the great kingdom of Nis2adha. He was a
<>devotee and worshipper of devas and Bra1hman2as. He
<>carried on trade and agriculture and by plundering
<>he amassed much wealth.
<NI>Hemakun2d2ala grew old. He thought about the frailty
<>of life and spent a sixth part of his wealth for charitable
<>purposes. For remission of the sins committed through-
<>out the whole of his life, he gave alms as stipulated
<>in the Pura1n2as. After entrusting the family affairs to
<>his sons S4ri1kun2d2ala and Vikun2d2ala, he went to the
<>forests for penance.
<NI>His sons were young. They turned away from
<>righteous ways and followed a path of pleasures and
<>wickedness. They refused to pay any heed to the
<>advice of their elders. Drinking and going to other
<>women became their routine.
<NI>Within a short time they lost their wealth. They had
<>nothing to eat. Their friends and favourites all discard-
<>ed them. Being forsaken by every body, they engaged
<>themselves in theft or robbery. They were afraid of
<>the king and the people, and so they shifted to the
<>forest. They lived by hunting. At this time the elder
<>brother was caught by a tiger. The younger brother
<>was bitten by a snake. Thus, on the same day, both
<>sinners met with death. The messengers of Yama took
<>both of them to the world of Yama. According to the
<>order of King Dharma, Vikun2d2ala got heaven and
<>S4ri1 Kun2d2ala got hell.
<NI>Vikun2d2ala who was glad at obtaining heaven asked the
<>men of Yama on the way, why he was given heaven.
<>They replied, “There was a Brahmin who was well-
<>versed in all branches of knowledge. He was the son
<>of Harimitra. His hermitage was on the southern
<>bank of Yamuna1. Yourself and the Brahmin became
<>friends in the forest. Because of that friendship you
<>were enabled to take bath in two Ma1gha months in
<>the holy waters of Ka1lindi1 which is capable of washing
<>all the sins away. By the first Ma1gha bath you got
<>remission of your sins. By the second Ma1gha-bath
<>you became eligible for the attainment of heaven.”

<HI>VINA1YAKA II. Gan2apati.
<HI>VINA1YAKACATURTHI1. One of the important festivals
<>of the Hindus. This is called the day of worship of
<>Gan2es4a. The Caturthi1 (4th day) of the bright lunar
<>fortnight in the month of Sim3ha is the birth day of
<>Gan2apati. It is a famous festival in North India. They
<>make the images of Gan2apati, every year, and make
<>offerings to them on this particular day.
<NI>It is believed, that he who sees the moon on Vina1yaka
<>Caturthi1, will be subjected to dishonour and derision.
<>This belief is based on the following story.
<NI>Gan2apati is very fond of sweetmeat especially Kozhuk-
<>kat2t2a (globular solid sweetmeat, called Modaka). It is
<>the custom in North India to worship Gan2apati by
<>offering these sweetmeats, even today, with all kinds
<>of festivities. On one birthday Gan2apati went from house
<>to house and ate belly-ful of modakas and returned
<>home on his conveyance, the rat. On the way the rat
<>saw a snake and began to tremble with fear. Due to
<>the shivering of its legs Gan2apati fell down. The belly
<>of Gan2apati was broken due to the fall and a large
<>quantity of modakas came out. Gan2apati gathered
<>everything that fell out of his belly and stuffed them
<>again in the stomach and joining the cut edges entwin-
<>ed the snake tightly round the stomach. Candra who
<>was standing in the sky seeing all these things laughed
<>with contempt. At this, Gan2apati got wild and plucked
<>his tusk and throwing it at the moon cursed him. “Let [Page857-a+ 65]
<>nobody look at you on the Gan2apati-festival day.”
<>(Brahmavaivarta Pura1n2a). This story is slightly differ-
<>ent according to Gan2es4a Pura1n2a. That story is, that
<>S4ri1 Parames4vara gave a plum to his elder son
<>Subrahman2ya without the knowledge of his younger son
<>Gan2apati, on the 4th day of a bright lunar fortnight
<>and the moon who smiled at it, was cursed.

<HI>VIPULA III. A hermit who was born in the dynasty of
<>Bhr2gu. There is a story showing how this hermit protect-
<>ed the wife of his teacher from Indra while he was the
<>disciple of the hermit Devas4arma1, in Maha1bha1rata,
<>Anus4a1sana Parva, Chapter 40. The story is given below:
<>Ruci, the wife of the hermit Devas4arma1, was extremely
<>beautiful. Devas4arma1 was aware of the fact that Indra
<>had often looked at his wife with covetous eyes. He had
<>to perform a sacrifice. But he feared that if he went
<>away from the hermitage his wife would be carried away
<>by Indra. At last he called his beloved disciple Vipula
<>and revealed the secret to him. The teacher told his dis-
<>ciple that Indra was a libertine as well as a magician
<>and that he would appear in various forms to entice
<>Ruci, and asked him to protect Ruci even at the cost
<>of his life. Then Devas4arma1 left the hermitage for the
<>sacrifice.
<NI>Vipula followed the wife of his teacher, wherever she
<>went. He feared that Indra might come even unseen by
<>anybody. So he decided to get inside Ruci by super-
<>natural powers of Yoga. He made Ruci to sit in front of
<>him and stare into his eyes and through the rays of her
<>eyes he entered inside her.
<NI>Knowing that Devas4arma1 had left the hermitage, Indra [Page858-b+ 64]
<>came in front of Ruci. By the power of Stambhana
<>(suppressing the use of faculties by mantra) Vipula
<>made Ruci stand motionless staring into the face of
<>Indra. She did not give any reply to the questions of
<>Indra. At last Indra looked into Ruci with inward eyes
<>and saw as in a mirror Vipula sitting inside her. With
<>shame Indra left the place instantly.
<NI>When the teacher returned on completion of the sacri-
<>fice Vipula told him all that had taken place. The
<>teacher was pleased and told his disciple that he might
<>ask for any boon.
<NI>He got the boon to be a righteous man throughout his
<>life and left the hermitage.
<NI>It was during this period that the marriage of Prabha1-
<>vati1, the sister of Ruci, took place. The marriage of
<>Prabha1vati1 with Citraratha, the king of An3ga, was settled.
<>A messenger from An3ga informed Ruci about it. Then
<>some flowers fell from the sky near Ruci. She wore
<>them and went to the marriage. Prabha1vati1 wanted to
<>have the same flowers. Vipula was sent to bring flowers
<>of the same kind. As Vipula was returning with the
<>flowers, he saw two men turning a wheel. Each of them
<>claimed that he had turned more than the other, and
<>quarrelled with each other. One of them pointing at
<>Vipula, said that he who told lies would get what Vipula
<>would undergo in hell. Vipula was worried at hearing
<>this. He proceeded on his journey. He saw six men gamb-
<>ling. One of them pointed at Vipula and said “A false
<>gamester would get what Vipula would get in hell.”
<>Being flurried by these two talks, Vipula ran to his
<>teacher to understand its meaning. He went to Campa1-
<>puri1 and saw the teacher and asked him the meaning of
<>what he had heard. The teacher told him, that the two
<>who turned the wheel were day and night and the six
<>who were engaged in gambling were the six R2tus (sea-
<>sons) and that R2tus and day and night are witnesses of
<>every sinful act committed any time. Vipula became
<>aware of his sin. While he was staying inside the wife of
<>his teacher, his genital touched her genital and face
<>touched face. He had not told the teacher this. But the
<>teacher said that it need not be considered a sin be-
<>cause the deed was done with no bad intention.

<>tection from the wife of Aviks2it. She being kind-hearted,

<>(Ma1rkan2d2eya Pura1n2a, Chapter 126).

<HI>VI1RABHADRA. One of the guards of S4iva.
<NI>1) {%Origin.%} There are two different opinions in the Pura1-
<>n2as, regarding the origin of Vi1rabhadra. There is no
<>doubt that his birth was due to the anger of S4iva. When
<>S4iva knew that his wife Pa1rvati1 jumped into the fire and
<>died at the sacrifice of Daks2a, he struck his matted hair
<>on the ground and from that, Vi1rabhadra and Bhadra-
<>ka1li1 came into being. This is the version given in Devi1
<>Bha1gavata, Skandha 7. According to Maha1bha1rata,
<>S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 284, Vi1rabhadra was born from
<>the mouth of S4iva. From each of the hairpores of Vi1ra-
<>bhadra, who was born from the mouth of S4iva to destroy
<>the sacrifice of Daks2a a fearful monster was born, all
<>of whom, formed a group of ghosts called the Raumyas.
<NI>2) {%The Destruction of the sacrifice of Daks2a.%} See under
<>Daks2a.
<NI>3) {%Attainment of boon.%} After the destruction of the sacri-
<>fice of Daks2a, the fearful monster Vi1rabhadra, began to
<>exterminate the entire creation. Then S4iva appeared
<>and pacified him and said “You shall become a planet
<>in the sky called An3garaks2aka (Bodyguard) or Man3gala
<>(well being). Everybody will worship you. Those who
<>thus exalt you, will get health, wealth and long life.”
<>(Bha1gavata, Skandha 7; Va1yu Pura1n2a, 101, 209; Padma
<>Pura1n2a, Sr2s2t2i Khan2d2a, 24).
<NI>After the destruction of the sacrifice of Daks2a, Vi1ra-
<>bhadra severed a portion of his radiance, and from that
<>radiance, later A1dis4an3kara (S4an3kara1ca1rya) was born.
<>This story occurs in Bhavis2ya Pura1n2a, Pratisarga Parva.
<NI>4) {%Prowess.%} Vi1rabhadra was not only a follower of
<>S4iva. He was a prominent general of the army. In the
<>battle of the burning of Tripura and the Jalandhara
<>fight, Vi1rabhadra stood with S4iva and fought fiercely.
<>(Padma Pura1n2a, Pa1ta1la Khan2d2a and Uttara Khan2d2a).
<NI>5) {%Protector of the Devas.%} Vi1rabhadra was the destroyer
<>of the Asuras and the protector of the Devas. Once [Page859-b+ 65]
<>Kas4yapa and all the other hermits and sages with him
<>were burnt to ashes in the wild fire that occurred in the
<>S4aukat2a mountain. Instantly Vi1rabhadra swallowed
<>that wild fire and by the power of incantation, he bro-
<>ught to life from the ashes all the R2s2is (hermits) who
<>were burnt to death.
<NI>On another occasion a serpent swallowed all the gods.
<>Vi1rabhadra killed the snake and rescued all the Devas.
<>Once an asura called Pan5camed2hra put into his mouth
<>all the gods, all the hermits and Ba1li and Sugri1va.
<>Those who escaped from the danger stood agape being
<>powerless to confront the Asura. At last Vi1rabhadra
<>attacked the asura. That great and fierce battle lasted
<>for years. At the end Vi1rabhadra killed the Asura and
<>rescued all.
<NI>Because Vi1rabhadra had thus protected the Devas and
<>the others on three occasions, S4iva became immensely
<>pleased with him and gave him several boons. (Padma
<>Pura1n2a, Pa1ta1la Khan2d2a, 107).
<HI>VIRA1DHA. A fierce Ra1ks2asa (giant) whom Ra1ma and
<>Laks2man2a killed in the Dan2d2aka forest. Vira1dha was
<>the rebirth of Tumburu, a Gandharva who had been
<>cursed to become a Ra1ks2asa. The story about S4ri1
<>Ra1ma's liberating the Gandharva from the curse and
<>sending him back to the world of Gandharvas, occurs
<>in Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a, Aran2ya Ka1n2d2a, Sargas 2 to 4,
<>as follows.
<NI>In days of old, Tumburu, a Gandharva had been serv-
<>ing Kubera. Once Tumburu was asked by Kubera to
<>bring Rambha1. Tumburu failed in bringing Rambha1
<>at the stipulated time. Kubera got angry and cursed
<>Tumburu to become a Ra1ks2asa. Tumburu requested
<>for liberation from the curse. Kubera granted his
<>request and said “In Treta1yuga, Maha1vis2n2u will
<>incarnate as S4ri1 Ra1ma, who with his sword will change
<>your Ra1ks2asa form. You will regain your former form
<>and will come back to the world of Gandharvas.”
<NI>Accordingly Tumburu took birth as the son of giant
<>Jaya. This child born to Jaya by his wife S4atahrada1,
<>grew up and came to be known by the name Vira1dha.
<>Two extra-ordinarily long hands and the outward
<>appearances of a giant aroused fear in every living
<>creature. He lived in the forest Dan2d2aka. It was at
<>this time that S4ri1 Ra1ma and Laks2man2a came with Si1ta1,
<>to live in this forest. As soon as Vira1dha saw them he
<>ran to them with a loud cry.
<NI>“With sunken eyes and swollen stomach, widened
<>mouth and an enormous body, with a fierce appearance,
<>of very great height an uncouth figure, body wet with
<>fat, clad in the hide of a leopard, looking like Yama
<>with open mouth, with three lions, two wolves, four
<>leopards, ten spotted deer and the head of a big tusker
<>with tusks smeared with fat, all these caught pierced
<>in an iron trident, and shouting in a roaring sound”,
<>he ran to them and after taking Si1ta1, he began to run.
<>Ra1ma and Laks2man2a followed him. Vira1dha placed
<>Si1ta1 down and, taking Ra1ma and Laks2man2a on each
<>of his shoulders he began running. Ra1ma and Laks2man2a
<>cut off each of his hands. But Vira1dha did not die.
<>Ra1ma and Laks2man2a decided to bury him alive.
<>Vira1dha recognized S4ri1 Ra1ma and told him his story.
<>Instantly his demoniac form changed and he regained
<>his original form of a Gandharva. Thus Tumburu
<>returned to the world of Devas. (See under Tumburu).

<HI>VIROCANA I.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} An asura. He was the son of
<>Prahla1da and the father of Maha1bali. Three sons Viro-
<>cana, Kumbha and Nikumbha were born to Prahla1da
<>by his wife Dhr2ti. Virocana, though an asura, perform-
<>ed rites and rituals carefully. He was kind towards
<>Brahmins. His son Bali became famous and got the
<>name Maha1bali. (M.B. A1di Parva, Chapter 65, Stanza
<>19).
<NI>2) {%Other details.%}
<NI>(i) Once there was a controversy between Virocana
<>and Sudhanva1. (See under Sudhanva1 II).
<NI>(ii) During the time of emperor Pr2thu, when the [Page862-a+ 64]
<>asuras milked the earth Virocana stood as the calf.
<>(M.B. Dron2a Parva, Chapter 69, Stanza 20).
<NI>(iii) Virocana is included among the ancient Kings of
<>prominence. (M.B. S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 227, Stanza
<>50).
<NI>(iv) There is a story about the quest for knowledge
<>about universal and individual souls, by Indra and
<>Virocana, in Cha1ndogyopanis2ad, as given below.
<NI>Once the Devas and the asuras approached Praja1pati
<>to learn about Brahman, the impersonal God. Praja1-
<>pati told them: “A1tman (soul) is the first tattva
<>(Essential being) which is sinless, eternal, desireless
<>and unimaginable in the earth.” Having heard this
<>philosophy about the soul, the Devas selected Indra,
<>and the asuras selected Virocana and to know the
<>details, they sent them to Praja1pati as his disciples.
<NI>Indra and Virocana stayed with Praja1pati for several
<>years to know more about A1tman. But Praja1pati did
<>not reveal to them the secret about Brahman. At last to
<>test them Praja1pati said “Your reflection that you see in
<>water or mirror is the A1tman (soul).”
<NI>Virocana, who mistook what the Praja1pati said as truth
<>immediately took his bath, put on costly dress and orna-
<>ments and stood near water and saw his reflection in water.
<>After that, taking the reflection for soul, he spread this
<>doctrine among his people. With this the asuras accept-
<>ed body as soul. But the Devas did not recognize this
<>philosophy. They accepted the doctrine that A1tman is
<>that essence of Nature which is alien to body and mind
<>and which is pure.
<NI>(v) There are two different statements about the death
<>of Virocana in the Pura1n2as.
<NI>(1) In the battle with Ta1raka1sura, Virocana was killed
<>by Devendra. (M.B. S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 99.
<>Brahma1n2d2a 1. 20. 35; Matsya: 10: 11; Padma Pura1n2a,
<>Sr2s2t2i Khan2d2a 16).
<NI>(2) The Sun God was pleased with Virocana and had
<>given him a crown. The sun told him that death would
<>come only if that crown was removed from the head by
<>some body. Because of this boon Virocana became
<>arrogant. So Maha1vis2n2u took the form of a beautiful
<>woman and enticed Virocana towards him and taking
<>away the crown killed him. (Gan2es4a Pura1n2a 2, 29).
<NI>According to Na1rada Pura1n2a, Maha1vis2n2u took the form
<>of a Brahmin and reached the palace of Virocana. There
<>changing the righteous wife of Virocana into a mad
<>woman he killed Virocana.
<NI>(vi) Virocana had two wives called Vis4a1la1ks2i1 and Devi1.
<>Two children, Bala and Ya odhara1 were born by them.

<HI>VIS2N2U.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} Brahma1, Vis2n2u and Mahes4vara
<>are the Lords of creation, sustenance and extermination
<>of this perishable universe. These trimu1rtis (three
<>figures) also are perishable. It is said, that one day of
<>Brahma1 will constitute thousand four-fold (catur) yugas
<>and that during the life of Brahma1, fourteen Indras will
<>fall down from heaven and die. This is a Brahma1 age.
<>The ages of two Brahma1s constitute the age of one Vis2n2u.
<>At the end of the age Vis2n2u also will perish. The age
<>of S4iva is double the age of Vis2n2u. S4iva also will perish
<>at the end of his age. (Devi1 Bha1gavata, Skandha 5).
<NI>When everything perishes there comes the deluge (the
<>great flood). After that, for one hundred and twenty
<>Brahma1 years the universe will be desolate and void. In
<>that deep eternal silence, Vis2n2u will be seen sleeping on
<>a banyan leaf on the surface of water. That is the
<>beginning of the next great age. In this stage, Ba1la-
<>mukunda is the name of Maha1vis2n2u. As he remains on
<>Na1ra or water he will be called Na1ra1yan2a also.
<NI>The name Vis2n2u means he who possesses the habit of
<>Vya1pana (To pervade). While Vis2n2u, who has the
<>power to spread his control over everything in whatever
<>condition, lies on the banyan-leaf. From his navel, a
<>lotus-stalk grows up, and on the top of the stalk, in the
<>lotus flower, Brahma1 comes into being. Brahma1 does
<>penance before Vis2n2u and extols him. Maha1vis2n2u confers
<>on Brahma1 the power of creation of the subjects. That
<>Brahma1 perishes along with the deluge and in his place
<>another Brahma1 is born. Thus in the life-time of Vis2n2u
<>two Brahma1s come into being and perish.
<NI>2) {%Beginning.%} In days of yore, when Vis2n2u was lying
<>on the banyan leaf as Ba1la Mukunda, he began to think
<>“Who am I? Who created me? Why? What have I
<>to perform?” -and soon an ethereal voice was heard,
<>“I am everything. Except me, there is nothing eternal.”
<>From behind the voice Maha1devi1 appeared, and said
<>“Look Vis2n2u. What is there to wonder at? Whenever
<>the universe is subject to creation, sustenance and
<>extermination, you have taken origin by the glory of
<>the Almighty. The Almighty or the omnipotence is
<>beyond attributes. But we are all subjected to attributes.
<>Your foremost attribute is Sattva (goodness-purity)
<>Brahma1 whose main attribute is the attribute of rajas
<>(activity-passions), will originate from your navel.
<>From the middle of the brows of that Brahma1, S4iva
<>will be born, whose main attribute is Tamas (inertia
<>darkness). Brahma1, by the power of Tapas (penance)
<>will acquire the power of creation and build the world.
<>You will be the sustainer of that world. S4iva will dest-
<>roy the same world. I am Devi1 Ma1ya1 (Illusion-
<>personified as the wife of Brahman), the great power
<>depending on you for the purpose of creation.” After
<>hearing these words of Devi1, Vis2n2u went into medita-
<>tion and deep sleep of contemplation.
<NI>3) {%Avata1ras (Incarnations).%} When injustice and law-
<>lessness abound in the universe, Vis2n2u will incarnate in
<>the world in various forms and shapes, and will drive
<>away injustice and will reinstate righteousness. The basis
<>and the indeclinable semen virile of all the incarnations,
<>is this spirit of the universe. All Devas, all human beings
<>and all animals are created from a portion of this soul
<>of the universe, which in itself is a portion. Brahma1,
<>first incarnated as Sanatkuma1ra and lived the life of a
<>Brahmin student of chaste abstinence. The second [Page864-b+ 65]
<>incarnation was connected with the creation of the
<>earth. It was the incarnation as a hog to redeem the
<>earth which was immersed in the world of Rasa1tala.
<>The third incarnation was taken to create the sages and
<>hermits. The Supreme God incarnated as the deva-
<>hermit, Na1rada and taught Pan5cara1tra, the Vais2n2ava-
<>s4a1stra explaining the ways of observing Karmans.
<>Fourthly, Vis2n2u took the incarnation of Nara-Na1ra1y-
<>an2as (two hermits) and performed tapas (penance),
<>difficult to do. The fifth incarnation was that of Kapila
<>who taught his disciple A1suri, a Brahmin, Sa1n3khya (one
<>of the six systems of Indian philosophy dealing with
<>evolution). The next incarnation was taken, according
<>to the request of Atri, as his son under the name
<>Datta1treya. Seventhly he took incarnation as Yajn5a, the
<>son born to Praja1pati Ruci, by his wife A1ku1ti with the
<>groups of devas (gods) such as Ya1mas and others to
<>sustain the Manvantara (age of Manu) of Sva1yam-
<>bhuva. The eighth incarnation was as the son of Bhaga-
<>va1n Na1bhi by his wife Meru, and the ninth was, as the
<>inner soul of Pr2thu, according to the request of the
<>sages and hermits, with a view to change the earth to
<>such a state that medicinal herbs may grow in plenty
<>everywhere. The tenth was, as Matsya (Fish) in
<>Ca1ks2us2a Manvantara deluge; the eleventh, as turtle,
<>to lift up the mountain Mandara; the twelfth as Dhan-
<>vantari, and the thirteenth was as Mohini1 (Charming
<>woman). The fourteenth was that of Man-lion, the
<>fifteenth was that of Va1mana, the sixteenth that of
<>Paras4ura1ma, the seventeenth, that of Vya1sa, the eight-
<>eenth, that of S4ri1 Ra1ma and the nineteenth was that of
<>Ra1ma and the twentieth that of Kr2s2n2a in the dynasty of
<>Vr2s2n2i. The twentyfirst was as Buddha in the beginning
<>of the age of Kali. The twenty second incarnation was
<>in the name of Kalki as the son of the Brahmin Vis2n2u-
<>yas4as. Each incarnation is explained in places where
<>that word occurs. See under Avata1ra.
<NI>The avata1ras of Maha1vis2n2u are numerous. Thousands
<>and thousands of incarnations originate from Maha1-
<>vis2n2u as streams flow from a lake which overflows at all
<>times. Hermits, Manus, Devas, Sons of Manus, Praja1-
<>patis, all these are marks and portions of Maha1vis2n2u.
<NI>(Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a, Ba1la Ka1n2d2a, Sar2ga 15; Agni
<>Pura1n2a, Chapter 5; Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a, Kis2kindha1
<>Ka1n2d2a, Sarga 40; Maha1bha1rata, Vana Parva, Chapter
<>83; Devi1 Bha1gavata, Skandha 1; M.B. S4a1nti Parva,
<>Chapter 121; Agni Pura1n2a, Chapter 12; Bha1gavata,
<>Skandha 10; Bha1gavata, Skandha 5; Maha1bha1rata,
<>Vana Parva, Chapter 272; Vana Parva, Chapter 149;
<>S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 339).
<NI>4) {%Family life.%} Vaikun2t2ha is the dwelling place of Maha1-
<>vis2n2u. Maha1laks2mi1 is the prominent wife. It is seen in
<>Devi1 Bha1gavata, Skandha 9, that besides Laksmi1devi1,
<>Gan3ga1 Devi1 and Sarasvati1 also were the wives of Vis2n2u.
<>Laks2mi1devi1 has taken several incarnations. Once she
<>took birth from Khya1ti, the wife of hermit Bhrgu. At
<>this birth Dha1ta1 and Vidha1ta1 were her brothers. On
<>another occasion, she arose from a lotus-flower which
<>grew up from the sea of Milk. (To know more about
<>the wives Laks2mi1, Gan3ga1 and Sarasvati1, see under
<>Gan3ga1).
<NI>There is none to be mentioned as the legitimate son of
<>Maha1vis2n2u. But Brahma1 is the first that could be
<>imagined as the son of Vis2n2u. Besides, Maha1vis2n2u once
<>created a bright son, by his mind. That son was named [Page865-a+ 64]
<>Virajas. S4a1sta1 is another son of Maha1vis2n2u. S4iva be-
<>came amorous with Mohini1 (fascinating woman)--the
<>form which Maha1vis2n2u took at the time of the churning
<>of the Sea of Milk. They led a short family life as a
<>result of which the son S4a1sta1 was born. (See under
<>S4a1sta1).
<NI>5) {%Curses.%} Maha1vis2n2u had cursed and had been cursed
<>on many an occasion. The most important of them are
<>given below:
<NI>(i) {%The curse of Maha1laks2mi1%} Once Maha1vis2n2u looked
<>into the face of Maha1laks2mi1 and laughed for no reason.
<>Thinking that Maha1vis2n2u had been making fun of her,
<>she cursed him saying “Let your head be severed from
<>the body.”
<NI>At this period an Asura named Hayagri1va had done
<>penance for a thousand years and obtained several boons.
<>One boon was that he should be killed only by a man with
<>the head of a horse. Hayagri1va attacked the devas (gods).
<>Though the gods fought with Hayagri1va for many thou-
<>sands of years they could not kill him. Even Vis2n2u,
<>admitted defeat. Using the bow as a prop to his chin he
<>stood thinking, for years. In the meanwhile white ants
<>began to eat the string of the bow. When the string
<>was broken, the bow straightened with a sudden jerk
<>and the head of Maha1vis2n2u was severed from the trunk
<>and was thrown away. Vis4vakarma1 cut off the head of
<>a horse and joined it to the trunk of Vis2n2u, who instant-
<>ly rose up and killed Hayagri1va. Thus satisfying the
<>need of the gods and making the curse of Laks2mi1 come
<>true, Vis2n2u regained his original form and returned to
<>Vaikun2t2ha. (Devi1 Bha1gavata, Skandha 1).
<NI>(ii) {%The curse of Bhr2gu.%} The Asuras who were defeated in
<>the war with Devas, approached Puloma1, the mother of
<>their teacher-priest S4ukra, and sought protection. Puloma1,
<>was the wife of hermit Bhr2gu. She began to do penance
<>for the destruction of devas. Knowing this Vis2n2u aimed
<>his weapon, the Discus, at her and killed her. Bhr2gu
<>got angry and cursed Vis2n2u to take birth as a man and
<>suffer the grief of separation from his wife for many
<>years. This curse was the first cause of the incarnation
<>of S4ri1 Ra1ma. (For details see under Bhr2gu, Para 4).
<NI>(iii) {%The curse of Vis2n2u.%} Once the handsome King Revan-
<>ta, mounted on the horse Uccais4s4ravas and came to
<>Vaikun2t2ha. Looking at the handsome youth, Laks2mi1
<>stood for a while enchanted by Revanta and his horse.
<NI>Maha1vis2n2u was displeased at this, and cursed her to
<>take birth on the earth as a mare. Accordingly she was
<>born as a mare and when the duration of the curse was
<>over returned to Vaikun2t2ha. (For details see under
<>Ekavi1ra).
<NI>(iv) {%The curse of Vr2nda1.%} See under Ma1ya1s4iva.
<NI>6) {%Contests and wars.%} Wars are very few in the Pura1n2as
<>in which Vis2n2u had not participated directly or indirect-
<>ly. As almost all of them have been dealt with in
<>various places in this book, they are not given here.
<>Only a few of the prominent among them are mentioned
<>here.
<NI>(i) {%Madhukait2abhas.%} Madhu and Kait2abha are two
<>asuras born from the ear-wax of Maha1vis2n2u. They
<>tried to attack Brahma1 and Vis2n2u killed them. (See
<>under Kait2abha).
<NI>(ii) {%Killing of Andhaka.%} Andhaka was a notorious asura.
<>He was the minister of Mahis2a1sura. When war broke
<>out between asuras and Devas, Andhaka caused havoc [Page865-b+ 65]
<>among the devas. At last in the fight with Vis2n2u
<>Andhaka was killed. (Devi1 Bha1gavata, Skandha 5).
<NI>(iii) {%Killing of Vr2tra1sura.%} See under Vr2tra.
<NI>(iv) {%Ra1hu.%} For the story of how Vis2n2u cut into two the
<>asura Ra1hu, see under Amr2tam.
<NI>(v) {%Contest with Brahma1.%} The story of Vis2n2u and
<>Brahma1 making a competitive journey to find out the
<>crest and foot of S4iva, is given with slight variations in
<>most of the Pura1n2as. (For detailed story see under
<>Brahma1, Para 5).
<NI>(vi) {%For the story of how Vis2n2u confronted the asuras Nemi,
<>Suma1li1 and Ma1lyava1n%} see under each of those words.
<NI>7) {%The weapons and ornaments of Vis2n2u.%} The following
<>are the prominent ornaments and weapons of Vis2n2u.
<NI>(i) {%S4ri1vatsa.%} This is a mark on the chest. It is said that
<>this is the mark imprinted by the angry Bhr2gu who
<>kicked on the chest of Maha1vis2n2u. (See under Bhr2gu).
<NI>(ii) {%Pa1n5cajanya.%} This is a white conch. Even by the
<>touch of this conch man becomes wise. (For further
<>details see under Pan5caja I).
<NI>(iii) {%The Discus Sudars4ana.%} Vajrana1bha is another
<>name of this weapon. Vis2n2u uses this weapon to deal
<>with fierce enemies. This is a wheel with a hole in the
<>centre and thousand arms going out from the centre.
<>The outer edge is sharp. This Sudars4ana Cakra
<>is operated by putting it on the first finger and turning
<>it round, and releasing it at the enemy. Though it is
<>terrible for the wicked and unjust, it forebodes good to
<>good people and so it is Sudars4ana (good to look at).
<NI>(iv) {%Kaumodaki1.%} This is the club. The syllable “Ku”
<>means the earth. Kumodaka means he who delights
<>the earth. He who makes the earth delightful is Vis2n2u.
<>As the club is the property of Kumodaka (Vis2n2u) it is
<>called Kaumodaki1.
<NI>(v) {%Kaustubha.%} This is the jewel of Maha1vis2n2u. (Ku =
<>the Earth. Stubhna1ti = Pervades (spreads). Kustubha =
<>ocean. Kaustubha-obtained from the sea. This jewel
<>obtained from the sea of milk at the time of its churn-
<>ing, is worn by Maha1vis2n2u on his neck. This is a red
<>Jacinth.
<NI>(vi) {%Nandaka.%} This is the sword of Vis2n2u. It is stated
<>in Maha1bha1rata, S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 166, that this
<>sword was obtained from Indra.
<NI>(vii) {%S4a1ran3g.%} This is the name of the bow of Vis2n2u.
<>This is called Vais2n2avaca1pa (the bow of Vis2n2u) also.
<>A description is given in Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a, Ba1la-
<>ka1n2d2a, Sarga 25, as to how this bow was obtained. It
<>is as follows:
<NI>Once the Devas made Vis2n2u and S4iva quarrel with each
<>other, to test their might. The fight between the two
<>began. Vis4vakarma1 gave each of them a bow. The bow
<>of Vis2n2u was called Vais2n2avaca1pa; the bow of S4iva
<>was called S4aivaca1pa. This Vais2n2avaca1pa is S4a1rn3ga.
<>Due to the power of S4a1rn3ga, S4iva was defeated in the
<>fight. Getting angry S4iva gave his bow to the King
<>Devara1ta of Videha. It was this bow that S4ri1 Ra1ma
<>broke at the time of the Svayam3vara marriage of Si1ta1.
<NI>After the fight, Vis2n2u gave his bow to R2ci1ka. That bow
<>changed hands from R2ci1ka to Jamadagni and from him
<>to Paras4ura1ma, who presented this bow to S4ri1 Ra1ma on
<>his return after the marriage with Si1ta1.
<NI>(viii) {%Vaijayanti1.%} This is the necklace of Vis2n2u. This
<>necklace, made of five jewels stuck together, is known
<>by the name Vanama1la1, also. Vis2n2u has a charioteer
<>named Da1ruka and four horses named S4aibya, Sugri1va, [Page866-a+ 64]
<>Meghapus2pa and Vala1haka. Garud2a is the conveyance
<>of Vis2n2u. He holds conch, discus, club and lotus in
<>each of his four hands. It is said that the discus was
<>made by Vis4vakarma1 with the dust of the Sun. In
<>Vis2n2u Pura1n2a particular mention is made about the
<>ornaments of Vis2n2u.
<NI>9) {%The names of Vis2n2u.%} The names of Vis2n2u given in
<>Amarakos4a and their meanings are given below.
<NI>1) Vis2n2u. He who is spread everywhere.
<NI>2) Na1ra1yan2a. (i) He who lies on water. (na1ram =
<>water). (ii) He who had adopted Na1ra (human body)
<>in incarnations. (iii) He who enters the human society
<>(Na1ra) as Ji1va1tma1 (individual soul).
<NI>3) Kr2s2n2a. (1) of dark complexion. (2) He who does
<>Kars2an2a (pulling or dragging) on the agha (sin) of
<>jagat (world).
<NI>4) Vaikun2t2ha. (1) The son of Vikun2t2ha1. There is an
<>incarnation as such. (2) At the time of creation twenty-
<>three Tattvas (essences-elements) did not join with one
<>another. So Vis2n2u joined earth to water, ether to air
<>and air to fire; Thus their individual existence was
<>made Vikun2tha-prevented. By achieving this he became
<>Vaikun2t2ha. (3) Vikun2t2ha means wisdom (knowledge).
<>So Vaikun2t2ha is he who has acquired knowledge. (4)
<>Vaikun2t2ha means holy basil (a herb). So Vaikun2t2ha is
<>he who wears rosary of holy basil. (5) Kun2t2ha means
<>Ma1ya1--Illusion. So Vaikun2t2ha is Ma1ya1 Maya or he
<>who is blended with Illusion. (the female creative
<>energy).
<NI>5) Vis2t2aras4ravas. (1) Vis2t2ara--tree--banyan tree. He
<>who is universally known as banyan tree. (2) Vis2t2ara--
<>a bundle of darbha grass. (Poa grass). He whose ear-
<>lobe is like this. (3) Vis2t2ara = is spread--He whose
<>fame is spread everywhere.
<NI>6) Da1modara. (1) Stomach is tied by a rope. (2)
<>Da1ma--names of the worlds. He who bears all the
<>worlds in his stomach. (3) He whose habit is dama or
<>self-restraint, is Da1modara.
<NI>7) Hr2s2i1kes4a--(1) The I1s4a-lord, of hr2s2i1kas--organs of
<>senses. (2) He who makes the world hr2s2ta--delighted--
<>bristling with his Kes4as--hairs.
<NI>8) Kes4ava (Ka-Brahma1. I1s4a-S4iva). (1) The Lord of
<>Brahma1 and S4iva. (2) He who has killed Kes4i1. (3)
<>He who has three Kes4as (heads) i.e. Brahma1-Vis2n2u-
<>I1s4a.
<NI>9) Ma1dhava. (1) Dhava-husband of Ma1-Laks2mi1. (2)
<>He who is born of the dynasty of Madhu. (3) He who
<>has killed Madhu.
<NI>10) Svabhu1. He who comes into existence by himself.
<NI>11) Daitya1ri the enemy of Daityas (the asuras, demons).
<NI>12) Pun2d2ari1ka1ks2a. (1) With aks2is-(eyes) like pun2d2a-
<>ri1ka-(lotus). (2) He who dwells in the lotus, that is
<>the heart of devotees.
<NI>13) Govinda. (1) He who lifted up the earth assuming
<>the form of a hog. (2) He who protects the heaven. (3)
<>He who redeemed the Vedas.
<NI>14) Garud2adhvaja. He whose ensign is Garud2a (Eagle).
<NI>15) Pi1ta1mbara. He who wears yellow silk.
<NI>16) Acyuta. He whose position has no displacement.
<NI>17) S4a1rn3gi1. He who has the bow called S4a1rn3ga.
<NI>18) Vis2vaksena. He whose army spreads.
<NI>19) Jana1rdana. (1) He who destroys janana-birth
<>(birth and death) (2) He who had destroyed the
<>asuras called Janas. [Page866-b+ 64]
<NI>20) Upendra. He who had become the younger brother
<>of Indra by taking birth as Va1mana.
<NI>21) Indra1varaja. Younger brother of Indra.
<NI>22) Cakrapa1n2i. He who has cakra--the weapon Discus
<>-in his hand.
<NI>23) Caturbhuja. He who has four hands.
<NI>24) Padmana1bha. He who has lotus in his navel.
<NI>25) Madhuripu. The enemy of the asura named Madhu.
<NI>26) Va1sudeva. (1) The son of Vasudeva. (2) He who
<>dwells in all living beings as individual soul.
<NI>27) Trivikrama. He who has measured the three worlds
<>in three steps. (In his avata1ra as Va1mana).
<NI>28) Devaki1nandana. The son of Devaki1.
<NI>29) S4auri. Born in the dynasty of S4u1rasena.
<NI>30) S4ri1pati. The husband of Laks2mi1.
<NI>31) Purus2ottama. The noblest of men.
<NI>32) Vanama1li1. He who wears the necklace which reach-
<>es up to the leg and is called Vanama1la1.
<NI>33) Balidhvam3si1. He who had killed the asura called
<>Bali.
<NI>34) Kam3sa1ra1ti. The ara1ti-(enemy) of Kam3sa.
<NI>35) Adhoks2aja. He who is not discernible to the organs
<>of senses.
<NI>36) Vis4vambhara. He who rules over the Vis4va (world).
<NI>37) Kait2abhajit. He who became victorious over
<>Kait2abha.
<NI>38) Vidhu. Expert in all things.
<NI>39) S4ri1vatsala1n5cchana. He who has the mark or scar of
<>S4ri1vatsa on his chest.
<NI>40) Pura1n2apurus2a. The earliest man.
<NI>41) Yajn5apurus2a. He who is remembered in ya1gas--
<>sacrifices.
<NI>42) Naraka1ntaka. He who had killed Naraka.
<NI>43) Jalas4a1yi1. He who lies in water.
<NI>44) Vis4varu1pa. One who has the cosmic form.
<NI>45) Mukunda. He who gives salvation.
<NI>46) Muramardana. He who had suppressed Mura.
<NI>10) {%Sahasra Na1mans.%} (Thousand names of Vis2n2u). The
<>list of thousand names of Vis2n2u, is present in Padma
<>Pura1n2a, Uttarakhan2d2a, Chapter 72. In Maha1bha1rata,
<>Anus4a1sana Parva, Chapter 149, also all the thousand
<>names are given. Variations are seen in these two lists.
<NI>11) {%Other details%} (i) Mention about Maha1vis2n2u occurs
<>in several places in R2gveda. But more prominence is
<>given to Indra. Though Vis2n2u is exalted in five R2gveda
<>mantras (incantations), when compared with other gods,
<>Vis2n2u is only a lesser god. The story of Trivikrama is
<>hinted in R2gveda. But there is no mention about the
<>incarnation of Va1mana or Maha1bali. R2gveda gives
<>Maha1vis2n2u only the position of a younger brother of
<>Indra. That is why the author of Amarakos4a has given
<>Vis2n2u synonyms such as Upendra, Indra1varaja etc.
<NI>(ii) Maha1vis2n2u was one of those who came to see
<>S4ivalin3ga (Phallus) when it was detached and fell down
<>at the curse of hermit Bhr2gu. (For details see under
<>S4iva).
<NI>(iii) Maha1vis2n2u gave Subrahman2ya as attendants two
<>Vidya1dharas named Vardhana and Nandana. (M.B.
<>S4alya Parva, Chapter 45, Stanza 37).
<NI>(iv) Maha1vis2n2u gave Subrahman2ya the necklace Vaija-
<>yanti1. (M.B. S4alya Parva, Chapter 45, Stanza 49).
<NI>(v) It is stated in Maha1bha1rata, Sabha1 Parva, Chapter
<>11, Stanza 25, that Maha1vis2n2u stays in the assembly of
<>Brahma1. [Page867-a+ 65]
<NI>(vi) Maha1vis2n2u showed grace to Uparicara vasu. (M.B.
<>S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 337, Stanza 33).
<NI>(vii) Maha1vis2n2u once took birth as the son of Aditi.
<>From that day onwards he got the name A1ditya also. (For
<>details see under Aditi). For further details regarding
<>Maha1vis2n2u, see under Vira1t2purus2a, Prakr2ti, Purus2a,
<>Brahmasr2s2t2i, Avata1ra, Amr2ta, Garud2a, Laks2mi1, Gan3ga1
<>etc.
<HI>VIS2N2UCITTA. A noble Vais2n2avite devotee, who lived
<>in Tamil Nadu. He lived in Villiputtur. It is said that
<>he was the incarnation of Garud2a. Vis2n2ucitta had ano-
<>ther name Periya1lva1r. A1n2d2a1l who was famous among
<>the A1lva1rs was the daughter of Vis2n2ucitta.
<NI>Vis2n2ucitta sang holy hymns in praise of the beloved
<>god. The hymns of praise he sang are called Palla1n2d2u.
<>He got the name Periya1lva1r or the foremost of the devo-
<>tees.
<NI>Once at Villiputtur, while he was getting beds ready to
<>plant holy basil, he was attracted by a divine infant. It
<>seemed to Vis2n2ucitta that the little girl was lying among
<>the basil plants. He took the child home and named
<>her Goda1. It was this Goda1 who became the famous
<>A1n2d2a1l later. Legends say that the birth of A1n2d2a1l was
<>in 97 Kali Era. Scholars say that Goda1 was born in the
<>middle of 7th century. There is another story which
<>mentions that A1n2d2a1l was born from a portion of
<>Goddess Earth.
<HI>VIS2N2UDA1SA. A Vais2n2avite devotee who lived in ancient
<>days. The story of this devotee who defeated his king
<>Cola in devotion to Vis2n2u, is given in Padma Pura1n2a,
<>Uttara Khan2d2a, Chapter 110. The story is as follows.
<NI>In days of old there was a king named Cola in Ka1n5ci1-
<>pura. It was because of his reign that the country got
<>the name Cola. He had performed several sacrifices.
<>On the banks of the river Ta1mraparn2i1, stood his golden
<>Yu1pas (pegs on which sacrificial animals were tied)
<>that the place looked like Caitraratha.
<NI>Once the king went to the temple and worshipped
<>Vis2n2u by offering flowers of gold and jewels such as
<>chalcedony and prostrated before Vis2n2u and rose up.
<>At that time a Brahmin named Vis2n2uda1sa from his own
<>city came there to worship, with holy basil and water
<>as offerings. He worshipped with the leaves and flower-
<>bunches of holy basil. Because of his worship by holy
<>basil, the king's worship by jewels, was dimmed. The
<>emperor got angry and said, “Vis2n2uda1sa, you are a poor
<>man who does not know how to worship Vis2n2u. What
<>merit has your worship of holy basil after mine of
<>jewels?” Both began to contest on this point. At last the
<>king said “Let us see who between us will get oneness
<>with Vis2n2u first, you or I”
<NI>After saying this the king went to his palace. He appoint-
<>ed Mudgala the high priest and began to perform a
<>sacrifice to Vis2n2u. The sacrifice was going on with
<>pomp and festivities. Vis2n2uda1sa also was immersed in
<>devotion to Vis2n2u to the best of his abilities.
<NI>Once Visn2uda1sa, after his usual prayer and meditation
<>prepared rice-food. But somebody took away the cook-
<>ed rice unseen by Vis2n2uda1sa. Fearing that he would
<>miss the time for his evening prayer, he did not think
<>of cooking food again. Next day also he cooked food
<>and went for evening prayer. On that day also the rice
<>was stolen. This continued. One day after cooking the
<>food, Vis2n2uda1sa waited close by in a hidden corner. He
<>saw a low-caste man who was a mere skeleton because of [Page867-b+ 65]
<>famine, stealing the cooked rice and feeling pity on him
<>he said, “Stop, stop. How can you eat it without any oily
<>thing? See, take this ghee also.” Saying so he drew
<>near. The out-caste was terrified at this and ran away.
<>On the way he stumbled and fell. Vis2n2uda1sa ran to
<>the spot and fanned him with his cloth. When he rose
<>up the figure in the place of the low-caste was that of
<>the real S4ri1 Na1ra1yan2a with conch, discus and club held
<>in his hands. Because of devotion Vis2n2uda1sa stood be-
<>numbed. While the King Cola and the people were look-
<>ing on, Vis2n2uda1sa got into the divine Vima1na and went
<>to the world of Vis2n2u.
<HI>VIS2N2UDATTA. Son of the Brahmin named Vasudatta.
<>The story of Vis2n2udatta is quoted to prove that bad
<>omens at the beginning of a journey is a warning that
<>the journey would not be fruitful and that it would be
<>rather dangerous.
<NI>When Vis2n2udatta became sixteen years old he decided
<>to go to the city of Valabhi1 for his education. Seven Brah-
<>min boys of his age gathered together and joined him.
<>Deciding not to separate from each other, they started for
<>Valabhi1, without the knowledge of their parents. When
<>they proceeded a little further they saw a bad omen.
<>Vis2n2udatta stood undecided, but the others pressed him
<>on and they continued their journey. Next day by even-
<>ing they reached a village of forest tribes. After walking
<>through the village they reached the house of a woman.
<>They got her permission to stay there for the night.
<>They all lay in a corner. Immediately all slept. Vis2n2u-
<>datta alone lay awake. When the night advanced, a
<>man entered the house. The woman and the man
<>talked for a while and carried on sexual sports, and
<>they lay together and slept. A light was burning in the
<>room. Vis2n2udatta saw everything through the cleavage
<>of the shutters, and thought. “I am sorry that we have
<>come to this house. He is not her husband. Sure! she is
<>a harlot.” As he was thinking thus, foot-steps were
<>heard in the courtyard. A young man fixed his
<>servants in their places. Then he entered the house and
<>saw Vis2n2udatta and his friends. The new-comer was
<>also a forest-man. He had a sword in his hand. He was
<>the owner of the house. Vis2n2udatta said that they were
<>travellers. When he heard it, without saying anything
<>he got inside and saw his wife sleeping with her lover.
<>With the sword in his hand, he cut off the head of the
<>lover. He did not kill the woman, who did not know
<>that her lover was killed. The forester laid the sword
<>down and lay in the same bed and slept. The light was
<>burning.
<NI>After a while the woman woke up, and saw her hus-
<>band who had cut her lover into two. She stood up
<>quickly and took the trunk of her lover and placed it
<>on her shoulder and taking the head in one hand, went
<>out and hid them in the pile of ashes. Then she return-
<>ed and lay down. Vis2n2udatta had followed her steal-
<>thily and seen what she had done. He also returned and
<>sat in the midst of his friends. She rose up and took the
<>sword of her husband and killed him with it. Then
<>coming out she cried aloud. “Oh dear! These travellers
<>have killed my husband.” The servants woke up and
<>came to the house and saw their master lying dead.
<>They tried to attack Vis2n2udatta and his friends.
<>Vis2n2udatta told them everything that he had seen, and
<>showed them the head and the trunk of her lover, hid-
<>den in the ashes. When they saw this they understood [Page868-a+ 64]
<>everything. They tried the woman. At last she admitted
<>the crime. They expelled her and drove her away. After
<>this the travellers returned to their homes. (Katha1sarit-
<>sa1gara, Madanaman5cuka1lambaka, Taran3ga 6).
<HI>VIS2N2UDHARMA1. A child of Garud2a. (Maha1bha1rata,
<>Udyoga Parva, Chapter 101, Stanza 13).
<HI>VIS2N2UJVARA. A great disease used by people to defeat
<>their enemies. The antidote for Vis2n2ujvara is S4iva-
<>jvara. In ancient days, in the fight between S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a
<>and Ba1n2a, S4ivajvara was sent against S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a by
<>Ba1n2a and to prevent it S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a sent Vis2n2ujvara
<>against Ba1n2a. (Bha1gavata, Skandha 10).
<HI>VIS2N2ULOKA. Vaikun2t2ha. It is mentioned in Devi1
<>Bha1gavata, Skandha 7, that this world is situated on
<>the top of Maha1 Meru along with the worlds of Indra,
<>Agni, Yama, S4iva, Brahma1 etc.
<HI>VIS2N2UMATI1. The queen of the king named
<>S4ata1ni1ka. Sahasra1ni1ka was the son born to Vis2n2umati1
<>and S4ata1ni1ka. (Katha1saritsa1gara, Katha1mukhalambaka,
<>Taran3ga 1).
<HI>VIS2N2UPADA. A place at the source of the river Gan3ga1
<>See under Gan3ga1.
<HI>VIS2N2UPADATI1RTHA. A holy place. It is stated in
<>Maha1bha1rata, Vana Parva, Chapter 83, that by bath-
<>ing in this place and worshipping Va1mana, one could
<>attain the world of Vis2n2u. This place is on the bank
<>of the river Vipa1s4a1. It is mentioned in Dron2a Parva,
<>Chapter 8, that Arjuna, in his dream, had travelled with
<>S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a to the world of S4iva and had, on the way,

<HI>VIS2N2UPAN5JARA. A Mantra (spell) taught to Devi1
<>Ka1tya1yani1 by S4iva. (See under Pa1rvati1).
<HI>VIS2N2UPU1JA1. (Form of worshipping Vis2n2u). There are
<>conventions regarding the form of worship of Vis2n2u
<>and his satellite gods. The general form of that worship
<>is given below:
<NI>Laks2mi1, Gan3ga1, Dha1ta1, Vidha1ta1, Yamuna1, Navanidhis
<>(nine treasures), Va1stupurus2a, S4akti, Ku1rma (turtle)
<>Ananta (serpent) and Pr2thivi1 (Earth) are the satellites
<>of Vis2n2u. First you must bow before Acyuta, (Vis2n2u)
<>with all his satellites. Then worship Dharma (Virtue)
<>Wisdom, self-renunciation, Supernatural power and
<>Lawlessness, Ignorance, Want of Self-renunciation and
<>want of supernatural powers, and then Bulb, Stalk,
<>Lotus, Filament and pericarp of the lotus and, the four
<>Vedas, four Yugas (ages) and the three attributes,
<>Sattva (purity) Rajas (passion) and Tamas (darkness).
<>After this the three Man2dalas (regions) of Arka (the Sun)
<>Soma (the Moon) and Vahni (fire). After this the nine
<>powers should be worshipped. Vimala1, Utkars2in2i1, Jn5a1na,
<>Kriya1, Yoga, Prahva, Satya, Ka1nti and I1s4a are the nine
<>powers. In the same way, Durga1, Sarasvati1, Gan2apati
<>and Ks2etrapa1la also should be worshipped. As the next
<>step heart, head, lock of hair, armour, eyes and the
<>weapons should be worshipped. Then worship the
<>conch, the Discus the club, the lotus, the mark S4ri1vatsa,
<>the Kaustubha, the Vanama1la1, the Earth, Guru and
<>Garud2a. With prayer and oblations offered to Indra,
<>Agni Yama, Nirr2ti, Varun2a, Va1yu, Kubera, I1s4a,
<>Ananta and Brahma1, who are the guardians of the ten
<>directions and the weapons and conveyance and
<>Kumuda and the others (the four mountains standing
<>near the Maha1 Meru) and Vis2vaksena (Vis2n2u) Vis2n2u-
<>pu1ja1 will be finished. By performing this worship of [Page868-b+ 65]
<>Vis2n2u and his satellites, one could attain all one's wish-

<HI>VIS2N2UPURA1N2A. One of the eighteen Pura1n2as. Vis2n2u

<HI>VIS2N2URA1TA. Another name of Pari1ks2it.
<HI>VIS2N2US4ARMA1. See under S4ivas4arma1.
<HI>VIS2N2UVRATA. A Vrata (fast or vow) taken thinking
<>of Vis2n2u in mind. By taking this vow, one could get
<>what one desires for.
<NI>Worship Vis2n2u, after bathing his image on the first day
<>of the vow of four days, beginning with the second day
<>of the bright lunar fortnight in the month of Paus2a,
<>with mustard; on the next day with gingelly seeds; on
<>the third day with Orris root and on the fourth day
<>with all the medicinal herbs. ‘All the medicinal herbs’,
<>means medicine such as Ma1n5ci1, Oris root, Costus,
<>Bitumen (stone juice), Saffron, Curcuma, bulb of
<>Kaccu1ri, Flower of Michelia Champaca and bulb of
<>Cyperus grass. After bathing the image as given above,
<>Vis2n2u must be exalted on the first day by the name
<>Kr2s2n2a, on the second day by the name Acyuta, on the
<>third day, by the name Ananta and on the fourth day,
<>by the name Hr2s2i1kes4a. The worship should be perform-
<>ed by offering flower, on the feet on the first day, on
<>the navel on the second day, on the eyes on the third
<>day and on the head on the fourth day, and Candra
<>should be given oblations and exalted by names such
<>as S4as4i1 on the first day, Candra on the second
<>day, S4as4a1n3ka on the third day and Indu on the fourth
<>day. It is ordained in Chapter 177, of Agni Pura1n2a,
<>that the worship of Vis2n2uvrata should be conducted in
<>this way. This is a form of worship observed by Kings,
<>women and Devas (gods).

<HI>VIS4VAKARMA1. The architect of the Devas.

<NI>The daughters of Vis4vakarma1:--The four prominent
<>daughters are Sam3jn5a1, Citra1n3gada1, Suru1pa1 and Bar-
<>his2mati1. The Sun married Sam3jn5a1. Sun got three

<>well-versed in Brahmavidya1 (theosophy). By the other
<>wife three other sons Uttama, Ta1masa and Raivata were
<>born to Priyavrata. These grew up to be famous and
<>gradually became lords of Manvantaras. This Priya-
<>vrata lived with his sons and ruled over the country
<>for eleven Arbuda ages (Arbuda = ten crores). In
<>spite of his old age, his faculties or his body did not
<>become weak. (Devi1 Bha1gavata, Skandha 8).
<NI>Citra1n3gada1 was the fourth daughter of Vis4vakarma1.
<>Ghr2ta1ci1 was her mother. The young and beautiful
<>Citra1n3gada1 one day went to bathe in the river in the
<>Naimis2a forest. When she got into the water the prince
<>Suratha, the son of King Sudeva came there. Their eyes
<>met. Both fell in love with each other. In spite of the
<>advice of her maids she succumbed to the desire of the
<>King. Knowing this her angry father Vis4vakarma1 came
<>to her and said, “Since you have deviated from the path
<>of righteousness and abandoned your soul to a libertine,
<>you will not have marriage, and hence you will not
<>enjoy the pleasures of having a husband or child.” As
<>soon as she was cursed, the river Sarasvati1 carried the
<>prince Suratha thirteen yojanas down along with her
<>current. Because the King was washed away by the
<>current Citra1n3gada1 fell down unconscious. The maids
<>sprinkled the water from the river Sarasvati1 on her face.
<>Still she lay there as dead. Thinking that she was dead,
<>her maids went in different ways to fetch firewood and
<>fire. When the maids were gone, she came to herself
<>and looked on all sides. Seeing none of her maids in
<>the vicinity, she felt miserable and jumped into the river
<>Sarasvati1, and the current carried her down and pushed
<>her into the great river Gomati1. Being aware of her
<>future, the great river Gomati1 pushed her down and
<>placed her in a big forest where lions, leopards, tigers
<>etc. lived in plenty.
<NI>A Guhyaka (a section of Yaks2as) who was going
<>through the sky, saw Citra1n3gada1 in the forest, and in
<>reply to his enquiry she told her story to him. Guhyaka
<>blessed her and advised her to go to the temple close
<>by and to worship S4ri1kan2t2hes4vara, so that every thing
<>might end well. Accordingly Citra1n3gada1 reached S4ri1-
<>kan2t2hes4vara on the south of Ka1lindi1, bathed in the
<>Yamuna1 at noon and went to the temple and bowed
<>before S4ri1kan2t2ha Mahes4vara.
<NI>At that time the hermit R2tadhvaja, well-versed in
<>Sa1maveda came there to bathe. The hermit called
<>Citra1n3gada1 and enquired about her. She told the hermit
<>all that had happened to her. Hearing her story, the
<>hermit became angry and cursed Vis4vakarma1. “Let
<>that Vis4vakarma1 who has behaved so cruelly towards
<>his own daughter become a monkey.” Then he called
<>Citra1n3gada1 and said to her. “Good girl, go to the holy [Page870-b+ 65]
<>place called Saptagoda1vara and worship Ha1t2akes4vara
<>Maha1deva. Devavati1, the daughter of the asura
<>Kanda1rama1li1 the hermit woman Damayanti1, the
<>daughter of A1n5jana, a Guhyaka, and Vedavati1 the
<>daughter of Parjanya would come there. At the
<>time when these three young women meet together
<>at Ha1t2akes4vara, you will unite with your husband.”
<>Being overjoyed at the words of the hermit, Citra1n3gada1
<>went to Saptagoda1vara, lived there and worshipped S4iva.
<>R2tadhvaja went on his way.
<NI>Vis4vakarma1, transformed into a huge monkey, was
<>causing havoc and devastation in the forest. Once the
<>five-year-old son of R2tadhvaja, called Ja1ba1li had gone
<>to bathe in the river. The Vis4vakarma1 monkey chased
<>this boy and caught him and taking him to the top of
<>a Banyan tree, placed him close to the branches and
<>tied him fast with creepers. After this the monkey went
<>to Maha1meru. As the second adventure, the monkey
<>separated Damayanti1 from her father An5jana, a
<>Guhyaka. Damayanti1 was born to An5jana by the
<>celestial maid Pramloca1. Hermit Mudgala had once
<>prophesied that this Damayanti1 would become the
<>prominent wife of a King. The delighted Damayanti1
<>was once about to get into the water of the holy bath
<>Hiran2vati1, with her maids when the Vis4vakarma1-monkey
<>ran to the spot and the terrified Damayanti1 jumped
<>into the river and was carried down by the current. She
<>floated down and got into a forest. It was in this forest
<>that Ja1ba1li was tied to the banyan branches. Damayanti1
<>saw Ja1ba1li. Each said to the other about the cruel deeds
<>of the monkey. After that according to the advice of
<>Ja1ba1li, Damayanti1 went to the temple of S4ri1kan2t2hes4vara
<>on the basin of the river Yamuna1. After worshipping
<>S4ri1kan2t2hes4vara, she wrote on the wall of the temple,
<>a poem about the misfortunes of herself and Ja1ba1li and
<>stayed in that place engaged in worshipping god.
<NI>The next confrontation of the monkey was with Vedavati1
<>the daughter of Parjanya. Vedavati1 was born to
<>Parjanya by a celestial woman Ghr2ta1ci1. Once while
<>Vedavati1 was playing in the forest, the monkey saw her.
<>He addressed her Devavati1, intentionally mispronouncing
<>her name. She replied, “You monkey. I am not
<>Devavati1, I am Vedavati1.” Instantly the monkey ran to
<>her. Vedavati1 quickly climbed on a hibiscus tree. The
<>monkey kicked at the tree and broke it. Vedavati1 held
<>fast to a strong branch of the tree. The monkey took
<>the branch and threw it on to the sea. Every movable
<>and immovable thing in the world thought a tree was
<>falling down from the sky. Seeing Vedavati1 falling
<>down, a Gandharva said, “Oh dear, Brahma1 himself
<>had said once that this damsel would become the chief
<>wife of Indradyumna, the famous hero, the son of Manu
<>the great King who has completed thousand ya1gas
<>(sacrifices).”
<NI>Hearing the words of the Gandharva, Indradyumna the
<>son of Manu, broke that branch into thousand pieces
<>by his arrows. Though the branch was destroyed, Indra-
<>dyumna could not find where Vedavati1 had fallen. She
<>floated into a part of the forest. All alone she walked
<>on and on and reached the temple of S4ri1kan2t2hes4vara,
<>on the bank of Yamuna1. Damayanti1 who had
<>reached the temple earlier and Vedavati1 met each other
<>and talked about their experiences. Thus due to the
<>wickedness of the Vis4vakarma1-monkey Ja1ba1li the son of
<>R2tadhvaja came to be tied, on to the banyan tree and [Page871-a+ 65]
<>Damayanti1 and Vedavati1 to be staying helpless in the
<>temple of S4ri1kan2thes4vara.
<NI>At this time the hermit Ga1lava reached the temple of
<>S4ri1kan2t2hes4vara. He saw Damayanti1 and Vedavati1 and
<>felt pity on them. Next day Ga1lava started for Sapta-
<>goda1vara to take a bath in Ka1rttika. Damayanti1 and
<>Vedavati1 followed the hermit. They reached Sapta-
<>goda1vara and dipped in Pus2kara bath. Under water
<>they saw several Virgin fishes gathered round a whale
<>begging him for love. The whale was saying harsh
<>words to them rejecting their request. The fish virgins
<>again told the whale. “Don't you see the hermit Ga1lava
<>going about with two beautiful damsels. If this right-
<>eous hermit does not fear slander, why should you, who
<>live under water fear it?” The whale replied. “Ga1lava
<>doesn't fear people because he is daring and blind with
<>love.” Hearing these words of the fishes, Ga1lava
<>became ashamed of himself. So without coming up he
<>stayed under water. The two girls finished bath and
<>got on the bank, and waited for Ga1lava. Vis4vakarma1's
<>daughter Citra1n3gada1, who had reached the place
<>earlier, met the two girls. They told each other their
<>stories. “As R2tadhvaja had prophesied, Damayanti1
<>the daughter of An5jana and Vedavati1 the daughter of
<>Parjanya have arrived.” Thought Citra1n3gada1. “If
<>Devavati1 the daughter of the asura Kanda1rama1li1, also is
<>come, I could unite with my husband Suratha.” Citra1-
<>n3gada1 became glad. At this time Devavati1, the daughter
<>of Kanda1rama1li1, ran to the spot, being chased by the
<>Vis4vakarma1 monkey.
<NI>The reader might remember that Damayanti1 had written
<>a poem on the wall of the temple at S4ri1kan2t2hes4vara
<>when she had gone there at the instruction of Ja1ba1li who
<>had been tied on to a branch of a tree. At noon on that
<>day R2tadhvaja had gone to the temple at S4ri1kan2t2hes4-
<>vara and happened to see the poem. Then only did he
<>understand that his son Ja1ba1li had been tied to a tree
<>by a monkey. By then five hundred years had elapsed.
<>R2tadhvaja was aware of the fact that the only person
<>capable of liberating Ja1ba1li, was S4akuni the son of Iks2v-
<>a1ku. R2tadhvaja reached Ayodhya1 instantly and told Iks2v-
<>a1ku. “Oh, mighty King! hear me, please! A monkey
<>has made my virtuous and learned son Ja1ba1li, a captive
<>and bound him on a tree, within the boundary of your
<>kingdom. Nobody in the world except your son S4akuni
<>will be capable of rescuing him.” S4akuni accompanied
<>R2tadhvaja to the forest. They saw the tall huge banyan
<>tree with bulky roots hanging on all sides and on the
<>top of the tree, on a lofty place, the son of R2tadhvaja
<>entangled and entwined by creepers. Seeing the net-
<>work of creepers around the body of the hermit's son,
<>S4akuni began to send arrows one after another and cut
<>off all the creeper's knots. R2tadhvaja climbed up the
<>tree. Seeing his father, Ja1ba1li bowed his head to his
<>father. R2tadhvaja was not capable of extricating his
<>son. The prince put down his bow and arrow and tried
<>to untie the knots of the creepers that held his body to
<>the branch. Though a sturdy man he could not do it.
<>At last they cut the branch close to his body and got
<>Ja1ba1li down. A piece of the branch was stuck to his
<>back. Thus with his son Ja1ba1li bearing a piece of lum-
<>ber on his back and S4akuni bearing bow and arrows,
<>R2tadhvaja came to Ka1lindi1.
<NI>R2tadhvaja, S4akuni and Ja1ba1li wandered about for years
<>in search of Damayanti1 and the others. After nearly a [Page871-b+ 64]
<>hundred years, with despair Ja1ba1li bearing the lumber
<>on his back, went with his father to Kosala. The king
<>of that country was Indradyumna, the son of Manu. He
<>welcomed the hermit with hospitality. R2tadhvaja talked
<>about Damayanti1. Indradyumna claimed that he had
<>once saved a young woman by his arrows from the
<>branch of a tree. They all started in search of the girls.
<>They reached Badarya1s4rama, where they saw a young
<>hermit. From the conversation it was revealed that the
<>young hermit was Suratha. When he learned everything
<>he stopped penance and accompanied them. Under the
<>leadership of R2tadhvaja, they reached Saptagoda1vara
<>and saw Citra1n3gada1.
<NI>In the meanwhile Ghr2ta1ci1, sad and miserable, was wan-
<>dering over the mountain of the rising sun, searching
<>for her lost daughter Citra1n3gada1. She met the cursed
<>monkey form of Vis4vakarma1 and asked it, “Oh! monkey!
<>have you seen a girl?” The monkey told her every thing
<>that took place. Ghr2ta1ci1 also reached Saptagoda1vara.
<>The monkey followed close behind her. As soon as
<>Ja1ba1li saw the monkey he got angry and jumped
<>forward to wreak vengeance. R2tadhvaja checked his
<>son and told him the history of Vis4vakarma1. The monkey
<>separated the piece of the branch from the back of
<>Ja1ba1li, who had been bearing it on his back for the last
<>thousand years. R2tadhvaja was immensely pleased at
<>this and asked the monkey what boon he wanted. The
<>monkey said. “Brahman, if you wish to give me a boon,
<>please recall your curse. Great hermit! I am Vis4vakarma1
<>the father of Citra1n3gada1. I became a monkey because
<>of your curse. Let all the sins I have incurred because
<>of the mischief of a monkey, be remitted.” Hearing
<>this R2tadhvaja said. “Your curse will end when you get
<>a strong and sturdy son by Ghr2ta1ci1.”
<NI>Hearing this Ghr2ta1ci1 rose up in the sky. The monkey
<>also jumped up and followed her. The monkey was
<>attracted by the beauty of Ghr2ta1ci1. Later, on the
<>mountain named Kola1hala, the monkey enticed Ghr2ta1ci1
<>and wooed her. She consented and they lived thus for
<>a long time. Then they went to the Vindhya mountain.
<>On the bank of the Goda1vari1, a sturdy son was born to
<>them. This son was the strong sturdy huge monkey Nala,
<>who helped S4ri1 Ra1ma.
<NI>On the birth of a son Vis4vakarma1 regained his former
<>form. He returned to Saptagoda1vara with Ghr2ta1ci1.
<>Ga1lava also came there. With the hermit Ga1lava at
<>the head, the priests made burnt offerings and began the
<>performance of the marriage ceremony. The Gandharvas
<>sang and the celestial maids danced. The first marriage
<>was between Devavati1 the daughter of Kanda1rama1li1 and
<>Ja1ba1li. Then Indradyumna married Vedavati1. Next,
<>S4akuni married Damayanti1, the daughter of An5jana,
<>and lastly Suratha married Citra1n3gada1. (Va1mana
<>Pura1n2a, Chapters 63 and 64).
<NI>3) {%Other details.%}
