<HI>VIS4VAKR2T. An eternal god (Vis4vadeva) concerned with
<>offerings to the Manes. (M.B. Anus4a1sana Parva, Chapter
<>91, Stanza 36).
<HI>VIS2VAKSENA I. An ancient hermit. It is mentioned
<>in Maha1bha1rata, Sabha1 Parva Da1ks2in2a1tyapa1t2ha, Chap-
<>ter 7, that he shines in the palace of Indra.
<HI>VIS2VAKSENA II. A synonym of Vis2n2u.
<HI>VIS4VA1MITRA. A royal hermit of immense attainments.
<NI>1) {%Genealogy.%} Descended from Brahma1 in the following
<>order Brahma1--Atri--Candra--Budha--Puru1ravas
<>-Vijaya--Hotraka--Jahnu--Puru--Bala1ka--Ajaka--
<>Kus4a--Kus4ana1bha--Ga1dhi--Vis4va1mitra.
<NI>2) {%Birth.%} Six beautiful daughters were born to Kus4a-
<>na1bha the son of King Kus4a. The hermit Brahmadatta
<>married them. After this a son named Ga1dhi was born
<>to Kus4ana1bha. Two children named Satyavati1 and
<>Vis4va1mitra were born to Ga1dhi. Satyavati1 was married
<>to R2ci1ka; As he was born in the family of the famous
<>king Kus4a, Vis4va1mitra got the name Kaus4ika also. His
<>kingdom was Ka1nyakubja. (Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a, Ba1la
<>Ka1n2d2a, Sarga 34).
<NI>3) {%Becoming a hermit.%} Vis4va1mitra and Vasis2t2ha were
<>two hermits who were hostile to each other throughout
<>their lives. A quarrel with Vasis2t2ha, persuaded
<>Vis4va1mitra to become a hermit.
<NI>(Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a, Ba1la Ka1n2d2a, Sarga 51). [Page872-b+ 64]
<NI>The hermit Vasis2t2ha erected his hermitage and did
<>penance in the country of Vis4va1mitra. Once, while
<>engaged in hunting Vis4va1mitra saw Nandini1 in the
<>hermitage of Vasis2t2ha, and wanted to have her. In the
<>battle which ensued between Vasis2t2ha and Vis4va1mitra,
<>the hermit Vasis2t2ha came out victorious. The ashamed
<>Vis4va1mitra gave up his kingdom and went to forest
<>to do penance. Vis4va1mitra became a royal hermit of
<>great attainments. There were constant confrontations
<>between the Ra1jars2i and the Brahmars2i (King-hermit
<>and Brahmin-hermit). (For the detailed story of the
<>quarrels between Vis4va1mitra and Vasis2t2ha see under
<>Vasis2t2ha, para 2).
<NI>4) {%Vis4va1mitra and Haris4candra.%} The histories of Vis4va1-
<>mitra, Vasis2t2ha and Haris4candra are intertwined as a
<>triple string. Vis4va1mitra made Haris4candra, the most
<>renowned of the men of veracity, go begging.
<NI>Haris4candra and Vis4va1mitra. Their history begins from
<>King Tris4an3ku of the Solar dynasty.
<NI>Formerly the name of Tris4an3ku was Satyavrata. Arun2a
<>was the father of Satyavrata. When Arun2a was reigning
<>the prince Satyavrata was leading a wicked life. He
<>once entered the wedding hall of a Brahmin and carried
<>away the bride by force. When the king knew this, he
<>expelled the prince from the palace. Vasis2t2ha, as the
<>family priest, was behind the cruelty on the part of the
<>king towards his son. It was because of this that Vis4va1-
<>mitra crossed the path of Satyavrata.
<NI>Satyavrata went to the forest and lived like a low-caste
<>man. King Arun2a repented his rashness. Entrusting his
<>kingdom to Vasis2t2ha, Arun2a went to the forest to do pen-
<>ance. For twelve years there was no rain in the country.
<>Famine broke out. Vis4va1mitra's wife and three children
<>were in great difficulty. The hermit had been engaged
<>in penance. So the wife of the hermit decided to sell
<>the middle son for the sake of maintaining the rest and
<>started for the market with her children. On
<>the way Satyavrata met them and learned the whole
<>story. He told her not to sell the child. He agreed to
<>give them food till the arrival of Vis4va1mitra. The agree-
<>ment was that he would tie the meat, obtained by hunt-
<>ing, to a tree outside the hermitage, every day. Satya-
<>vrata carried out the promise. One day he did not get
<>anything from hunting. He caught hold of Vasis2t2ha's
<>cow which had been grazing in the forest and killed it
<>and gave its flesh to the family of Vis4va1mitra. On com-
<>ing to know this Vasis2t2ha cursed him and changed his
<>form into that of a can2d2a1la (low-caste). Moreover, as
<>he had incurred three sins such as stealing of a bride,
<>anger of father and cow-slaughter, he came to be
<>called Tris4an3ku from that day onwards. Weighed down
<>by these sins, he tried to commit suicide. Devi1 appeared
<>before him and gave him back his original form and
<>his kingdom.
<NI>After the death of Arun2a, Tris4an3ku assumed the reign.
<>Haris4candra was his son. After giving the country to his
<>son, Tris4an3ku requested Vasis2t2ha to perform the sacrifice
<>to send him to heaven bodily. Vasis2t2ha said that it was
<>impossible for him. Vasis2t2ha's enemy Vis4va1mitra took
<>up the task. He lifted Tris4an3ku bodily, up to heaven.
<>But he was denied admittance in heaven and so Vis4va1-
<>mitra created an artificial heaven between the earth
<>and heaven and made Tris4an3ku stay there.
<NI>Vis4va1mitra was keeping up hostile attitude towards the [Page873-a+ 65]
<>kings of the Solar dynasty. In reality it was not the
<>hostility towards the Solar dynasty, but it was his
<>enmity against Vasis2t2ha. Vis4va1mitra did not like
<>Vasis2t2ha's being the family-priest of the kings of the
<>Solar dynasty. So Vis4va1mitra kept up an attitude of
<>antipathy towards them. This is the background of the
<>quarrel between Haris4candra and Vis4va1mitra.
<NI>Haris4candra took Candramati1, the daughter of S4ibi,
<>as his first wife. Besides her, he had ninetynine wives.
<>But they had no children. At last according to the
<>advice of Vasis2t2ha he went to the basin of the Ganges
<>and did penance before Varun2a. Vis4va1mitra did not
<>like this. Varun2a appeared and said that Haris4candra
<>would get a son. The king had promised that he would
<>give his son as a sacrificial animal to Varun2a.
<NI>Candramati1 became pregnant and delivered a son. He
<>was named Rohita1s4va. Even after the lapse of a month,
<>the son was not given to Varun2a. On several occasions
<>Varun2a demanded the child; and Haris4candra would
<>give some excuses. Finally the king agreed to hand
<>him over to Varun2a at the age of eleven after his
<>Upanayana (investiture with the Brahma string). The
<>boy completed his tenth year. Preparations were being
<>made in the palace, for Upanayana, when Varun2a
<>arrived. The prince, who was aware of the fact that his
<>father would sacrifice him after his Upanayana, ran
<>away from the palace at night. Varun2a asked the king
<>to hand over the boy to him. The king was in great
<>perplexity. Varun2a cursed the king that he would catch
<>the disease called Jalodara (dropsy). Thus the king be-
<>came a sick man. Rohita1s4va heard from travellers that
<>his father was ill. On many occasions he wanted to
<>return to the palace. But Indra appeared before him in
<>the form of a Brahmin and dissuaded him from
<>going to the palace.
<NI>Haris4candra called Vasis2t2ha and asked him to suggest
<>a remedy for this woe and misery. Vasis2t2ha advised
<>him to fulfil somehow or other, the promise made to
<>Varun2a. The hermit continued. “Sons are of ten types.
<>A son bought for price also is included in this. So it
<>is enough if a son is bought for price and is sacrificed.
<>Some Brahmin may be found, who will be willing to sell
<>his son. If you please Varun2a thus, you will be cured.”
<NI>The King was delighted to hear this. He instruct-
<>ed his minister to find out any Brahmin who was will-
<>ing to sell his son. A greedy Brahmin was found out.
<>His name was Aji1garta. He had three sons. He was
<>prepared to sell the second son, S4unas4s4epha. The minister
<>agreed to give him hundred cows in return.
<NI>Up to this time Vis4va1mitra had been waging only a
<>shadow war against the Kings of the Solar dynasty.
<>From this moment he entered the scene of war. The
<>minister bought S4unas4s4epha and brought him to the
<>palace. Vis4va1mitra also arrived at the palace. He
<>sympathised with S4unas4s4epha who was crying pitiably.
<>He asked the King to release the boy, and gave a
<>warning that if the boy was not set free, the sacrifice
<>would be obstructed. The King said that he was doing
<>so to get recovery from illness, that he would give Vis4va1-
<>mitra a good deal of wealth, and requested him not to
<>cause any hindrance to the sacrifice. These words and
<>the misery of the boy kindled the anger of Vis4va1mitra.
<>He called S4unas4s4epha and taught him Varun2amantra
<>(spell) and told him to repeat the mantra when he was
<>lying on the slaughter-stone and that he would escape [Page873-b+ 65]
<>death. S4unas4s4epha did as he was told. Varun2a became
<>pleased with him and appearing before the King said,
<>“Leave S4unas4s4epha and perform the sacrifice. You will
<>get recovery.” Saying so Varun2a disappeared. Immedi-
<>ately the King was cured of his disease. At the order of
<>the King S4unas4s4epha was set free. The sound ‘Jaya Jaya’
<>(victory) reverberated in the sacrificial hall. S4unas4s4epha
<>got up and asked. “Oh great men. Who is my father
<>now? Some said that it was Aji1garta. Some others
<>argued that it was Haris4candra. Some said that it was
<>Varun2a.” At this time Vasis2t2ha stood up and said.
<>“Oh, great men, please stop arguing. I shall give reply
<>in accordance with the convention of Vedas. When he
<>bargained on the price of his son and received the cost
<>Aji1garta lost his paternity. Thenceforward Haris4candra
<>who bought the boy became his father. From the
<>moment he had issued orders to bind the boy and place
<>him on the slaughter-stone, he also had lost his paternity.
<>The claim of Varun2a to his paternity, because the boy
<>had been saved from death by him, does not hold good.
<>Any god will be pleased, when praised and glorified
<>with great laudatory mantras and will confer upon the
<>supplicant wealth, life, cow, land, salvation etc. There
<>is nothing unusual in this. But it was Vis4va1mitra who
<>taught him the Varun2a-spell in his pitiable and danger-
<>ous situation. So Vis4va1mitra alone has claim to the
<>boy's paternity.”
<NI>Those who were present, accepted this decision.
<>Immediately Vis4va1mitra took S4unas4s4epha with him and
<>went to his hermitage. Hearing about the recovery of
<>the King, Rohita1s4va returned to the palace from the
<>forest. Haris4candra received him with tears of joy. The
<>King, with his wife and son led a happy life and ruled
<>over his subjects with justice and truth. At this time,
<>Haris4candra (of Kakutstha's family) accepting Vasis2t2ha
<>as the main priest performed the famous sacrifice of
<>Ra1jasu1ya (Royal) consecration with ceremonies and
<>festivities. With this the fame of Haris4candra spread
<>far and wide.
<NI>At this point begins the next stage of confrontation
<>between Vis4va1mitra and Haris4candra. Vasis2t2ha once
<>reached heaven. Vis4va1mitra also reached there at the
<>same time. The devas greeted both honourably. But
<>Vis4va1mitra saw that Vasis2t2ha was shown some parti-
<>ality. This was unpalatable to Vis4va1mitra, who asked
<>Vasis2t2ha. “What excellence have you, more than I?”
<>Vasis2t2ha replied. ‘Have you not heard about Haris4-
<>candra, the King of the Solar dynasty? It is the noblest
<>dynasty in the world. The familypriesthood of this
<>dynasty also is laudable. My disciple Haris4candra of
<>that royal family has recently performed the sacrifice of
<>Ra1jasu1ya. I was the Supreme priest of the function.
<>This is a covetable position not attainable to many.
<>Moreover, there is none in the world, more truthful,
<>firm of character, more charitable and more liberal than
<>Haris4candra. This is a fact.”
<NI>Vis4va1mitra got up angrily and aruged that Haris4-
<>candra was not truthful. He staked all the fruits of
<>his penance to prove this. From that day onwards Vis4va1-
<>mitra began to make moves to instigate Haris4candra to
<>deviate from the path of truth.
<NI>Once Haris4candra, while he was hunting, met a lonely
<>woman in the forest. She was moaning. The King
<>asked why she was lamenting. She replied. “Oh King.
<>I am Siddhiru1pin2i1 (a goddess who helps people to attain [Page874-a+ 65]
<>anything). Vis4va1mitra is doing penance to possess me. I
<>request you to protect me.” The King promised her to
<>see that she was not subjected to the molestation of
<>Vis4va1mitra any longer. After that Haris4candra went to
<>the hermitage of Vis4va1mitra and made an enquiry. He
<>then asked the hermit to stop penance, as his severe,
<>intense, penance was harmful to many people in the
<>country. The King returned to the palace. Vis4va1mitra
<>got angry and stood up. Up to this time only a cold war
<>existed between them. Hostility became open now.
<NI>Vis4va1mitra began to make moves against Haris4candra
<>quickly. He changed a fierce asura into a hog and sent
<>it to the garden of Haris4candra. The hog destroyed the
<>garden. All the attempts made by the guards to drive
<>the hog away ended in failure. They informed the King.
<>The King mounted on a horse and with weapons
<>started for the garden. Without paying any heed to
<>the arrows of the King, the hog ran away. The King
<>began to chase it. The hog seemed to be near. Then it
<>was away, then in front of the King and suddenly it
<>appeared behind him. Then it would disappear
<>instantly. In this manner the hog played around the
<>King. After a while, the King was separated from his
<>army and was entrapped, all alone, in a thick forest. He
<>did not find any way out. He lost his way in the forest.
<>As he was thus walking slowly, he saw a stream of pure
<>water in front of him. Both the King and the horse drank
<>from the stream. As he was standing thus without know-
<>ing the way to return home, Vis4va1mitra went to him in
<>the guise of an old Brahmin.
<NI>The King honoured the old man, and told him that he
<>was Haris4candra, the King of Ayodhya1, and that by
<>chasing a hog which destroyed his garden, he had
<>reached the forest. He continued telling the old Brahmin
<>who had helped him. “You might have heard that
<>Haris4candra, the King of Ayodhya1, had performed the
<>sacrifice Ra1jasu1ya. I am that same King. It is my vow
<>to give anybody what he asks for. If you want money
<>or anything for sacrifice or for any other purpose, just
<>come to Ayodhya1. I will give you whatever you want.”
<>The old man was pleased. He told the King that the
<>jungle-stream flowed through a holy place and that
<>it would be better to offer the gift after taking a bath
<>in the river. The King purified himself by bathing in
<>the river and then said. “Sir, I am ready to offer gifts.
<>State your needs. It is my vow to give what is requested.
<>At the time of the Ra1jasu1ya I acted so towards all of
<>you and took a vow that I would do so in future also. I
<>am glad because I have met you on the bank of this
<>holy stream. So tell me quickly what you want.”
<NI>Brahmin:--“Oh King, I have heard about your fame.
<>Moreover there is nobody in the world equal to Haris4-
<>candra, born of the Solar dynasty, the son of Tris4an3ku
<>in liberality. Such is the opinion of hermit Vasis2t2ha.
<>There is nothing more to know about you, oh, King,
<>who is such a man of liberality. I have only one desire.
<>The marriage of my son is being conducted. I do not
<>possess enough money for the marriage. I want only a
<>help for the same.” The King thought it to be a very
<>simple request, and promised to give the required
<>amount. Vis4va1mitra by illusion customary to Gandharvas
<>created a young man and a young woman, and showed
<>them to the King saying that they were his son and
<>daughter. Then the Brahmin who was delighted by the
<>promise, showed the King the way to the palace. [Page874-b+ 65]
<>After making all arrangements for the marriage, Vis4va1-
<>mitra approached King Haris4candra. The King asked
<>him what amount he required. “Give me your kingdom
<>with all the elephants, horses, chariots, jewels and
<>wealth in it”, said Vis4va1mitra. The King who had
<>been led to this deception by Vis4va1mitra, having no go,
<>agreed. Thus Vis4va1mitra obtained the kingdom and
<>everything that Haris4candra possessed. It is conven-
<>tional that whenever a gift is given to Brahmins, a
<>daks2in2a1 (monetary gift) also should be given along
<>with it. Otherwise the gift will be futile. The King
<>asked the Brahmin what he wanted as daks2in2a1. He
<>demanded two and a half Bha1ras of gold as daks2in2a1.
<>The King agreed to give that also. But where to get
<>this amount from, since he had lost his kingdom and
<>everything? Having sunk deep in misery due to the
<>deceit of Vis4va1mitra, the King sat on the soil, cursing
<>his fate. Seeing this, the queen ran to him and cried.
<>While he was telling his wife every thing, Vis4va1mitra
<>came there and said:
<NI>Vis4va1mitra:--“Hariscandra! According to the gift
<>hand over your country and everything instantly. I
<>must have the daks2in2a1 of two and a half Bha1ras of gold
<>also just now.”
<NI>Haris4candra:--“Sir! According to my promise receive
<>everything now. We are leaving the country instantly.
<>But since I have given you everything that I had, how
<>can I give you daks2in2a1? Everything I had, has become
<>yours. The amount for daks2in2a1 has yet to be procured.
<>So receive the gift now. The daks2in2a1 shall be given as
<>early as possible.”
<NI>After giving everything to the hermit, the King left the
<>country with only the cloth he had been wearing. His
<>wife and child followed him. The hermit also follow-
<>ed the King compelling him to give him the daks2in2a1.
<>The King told him that only after paying this debt
<>would he eat any food, and that he would pay the
<>amount within a month. Vis4va1mitra, unwillingly agreed
<>to this.
<NI>With his wife Candramati1 and his young son, Haris4-
<>candra reached Ka1s4i1. After a month Vis4va1mitra came
<>to Ka1s4i1 for the amount of daks2in2a1. Finding no go,
<>Candramati1 said to her husband. “My Lord! sell me to
<>some one and clear off this debt.” The King with tears
<>agreed to this proposal. Because of their woe and
<>misery, both fell on the ground and fainted. The child
<>sat near them hungry and crying. Vis4va1mitra stood near
<>them compelling them to pay the amount. When Haris4-
<>candra came to himself, he sold his beloved wife to a
<>Brahmin in the village close by. The Brahmin who
<>bought Candramati1 was Vis4va1mitra. Haris4candra was
<>not aware of this. After counting out a crore of gold
<>pieces in a cloth and placing it on the ground Vis4va1-
<>mitra caught hold of Candramati1 by her hair and
<>dragged her away. He bought the crying child also
<>paying its price. The Brahmin led the mother and the
<>child, beating and dragging them along, like animals.
<>They disappeared from the sight of the King.
<NI>Vis4va1mitra again came before Haris4candra and asked
<>for the money. Haris4candra gave Vis4va1mitra, all the
<>money he got. The hermit was not satisfied. Vis4va1mitra
<>said that the money given, was not an adequate amount
<>as daks2in2a1 when the importance of the great sacrifice
<>Ra1jasu1ya was considered and that if he was to get the
<>full benefit of the sacrifice he had to satisfy him by [Page875-a+ 65]
<>giving him the requisite amount. The King accepted
<>everything the hermit said without any objection.
<>Vis4va1mitra compelled him for payment. The King
<>requested for time. Vis4va1mitra allowed time till sunset
<>that day.
<NI>As soon as Vis4va1mitra had gone Haris4candra walked
<>on with bent head, calling out. “Does anybody want
<>me? Will anybody buy me for price?” Instantly
<>Yamadharma came there as an outcaste and bought
<>Haris4candra. The name of the outcaste was Pravi1ra.
<>He bought Haris4candra to guard the funeral ground
<>and to collect tax on dead bodies. Vis4va1mitra quickly
<>ran to the place. The outcaste gave Vis4va1mitra ten
<>yojanas of land which yielded jewels, in the region of
<>Praya1ga and severed his connection. Vis4va1mitra went
<>on his way. The outcaste King took Haris4candra to
<>the funeral ground. Day and night Haris4candra had to
<>guard the entrance of the funeral ground.
<NI>At this juncture Haris4candra's son died of snake bite,
<>while he was playing with other children on the bank
<>of the Ganges. His mother Candramati1 fainted and
<>fell down, the moment she heard about it. As soon as
<>she recovered, she lamented over the death of her son
<>for a long time. Then she requested her master for
<>permission to go and see the dead body of her son. But
<>she was not given permission. She repeatedly pleaded
<>crying all the while. Then the Brahmin, her master, got
<>angry and said. “You slave! If your son it dead, let
<>him be dead. Is it any loss to you? It is my money
<>that is lost. You go and do your work. If not I will
<>operate this whip well on you. Remember that. You
<>know the biting pain of this whip. Stop wailing and
<>lamenting.”
<NI>Candramati1 persisted in her request to allow her to go
<>and see the dead body of her son. Not only did he
<>refuse to allow her to see the dead body of her son, but
<>also beat her. With tears she turned to her duties. It
<>was night. The Brahmin took his meals and lay down
<>to sleep. Candramati1 was sitting at his feet massaging
<>his legs. When it was nearly midnight that stone-hearted
<>old Brahmin said. “Now you may go. Complete the
<>funeral and return before dawn. Your usual work in the
<>morning should not be left undone. If so, you know
<>the consequences.”
<NI>Hearing these words, Candramati1 ran to the place
<>where the dead body of her son lay. The son lay on the
<>grass dead and stiff, with the face and body turned blue
<>due to poison. She saw that face in the flash of a light-
<>ning. She cried aloud. Hearing the cry people of the
<>neighbouring houses ran to the spot. Candramati1 did
<>not give any reply to their questions Some thought her
<>to be a ghost. Some wanted to kill her. Some caught
<>her by the hair. Some struck at her. At last they tied
<>her with a rope and dragged her to the funeral place.
<>They asked Haris4candra who was standing there, to
<>cut her into pieces. He refused to kill a woman. The
<>outcaste King came there and giving Haris4candra a big
<>sword asked him again and again to cut her into pieces.
<>Candramati1 and Haris4candra did not recognize each
<>other. At last, finding it difficult to disobey his master,
<>Haris4candra raised the sword to cut her.
<NI>Then Candramati1 shouted. “You outcaste. My son is
<>lying dead on the bank of the Ganges near this town.
<>Let me bring his body and cremate it. Allow me this
<>much time. After that I will come and sit here to be [Page875-b+ 65]
<>cut into pieces by you.” Haris4candra agreed to it. Crying
<>all the way Candramati1 went to the bank of the Ganges
<>and brought the dead body of her son to the cremation
<>place. Seeing her pitiable condition Haris4candra went
<>close to the dead body and removing the shroud looked
<>at the corpse. Because of poison the body of the child
<>was blue and ugly and as Haris4candra and Candramati1
<>had undergone so thorough a change they did not
<>recognize each other. But from her lamentation and
<>talk, he understood that the woman was his wife
<>Candramati1. He also cried aloud. Candramati1 recogniz-
<>ed her husband. Still Haris4candra said that if the
<>child was cremated without collecting the usual fee, it
<>would be deceiving his master. At last both of them
<>decided to commit suicide before the night ended.
<NI>Without loss of time Haris4candra gathered half-burned
<>fire-wood, and built a pile big enough to burn the
<>child's body and for them to jump into it. He laid the
<>child on it and set fire to it. Haris4candra and Candra-
<>mati1 stood with closed eyes ready to jump into the
<>burning fire. Then Brahma1 appeared there and pre-
<>vented them from jumping into the fire. Indra and the
<>Devas showered Amr2ta (Ambrosia). The child came to
<>life and got out of the fire. The King and the queen re-
<>gained their shining bodies and royal garments and
<>ornaments. The outcaste who was the master of Haris4-
<>candra was really, Dharmadeva. All the Devas blessed
<>Haris4candra and Vis4va1mitra returned the kingdom to
<>the truthful Haris4candra. Their subjects were overjoyed
<>at the return of their King and queen. After that Rohita
<>was anointed as the King of Ayodhya1 and the Devas
<>went with Haris4candra to heaven. (Devi1 Bha1gavata,
<>Skandha 7).
<NI>6) {%Vis4va1mitra and the brothers Ra1ma and Laks2man2a.%} See
<>under Ra1ma, Paras 5, 6, 7 and 8.
<NI>7) {%Weapon Training.%} Vis4va1mitra had proficiency in wield-
<>ing all types of weapons. He taught Ra1ma and Laks2man2a
<>all that he knew about weapons. See under Astra.
<NI>8) {%Cursing Rambha1.%} Once Vis4va1mitra was doing very
<>severe penance. Indra feared him. So wishing to hinder
<>the penance of Vis4va1mitra somehow Indra called
<>Rambha1 to him and said to her. “Rambha1, you dress
<>well and dance before Vis4va1mitra. Somehow his pen-
<>ance must be hindered. I shall take the form of a
<>cuckoo, and help you by singing.”
<NI>Indra and Rambha1 reached the forest of penance. The
<>cuckoo began to sing and there was the atmosphere of
<>spring season. Rambha1 danced before Vis4va1mitra. The
<>concentration of the hermit was broken. The hermit got
<>angry and cursed Rambha1 and changed her into a rock.
<>She entreated for redemption from the curse. The her-
<>mit told her that after ten thousand years a Brahmin
<>named Bhu1ritejas would touch the rock, by which touch
<>she would get her original form. (Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1yan2a,
<>Ba1laka1n2d2a, Sarga 64).
<NI>9) {%Vis4va1mitra and Tris4an3ku.%} See under Tris4an3ku.
<NI>10) {%Vis4va1mitra and Menaka1.%} See under S4akuntala1 and
<>Kadali1garbha1.
<NI>11) {%Cursing Vidyutprabha1.%} Once Vis4va1mitra did penance
<>to obtain the position of Kubera, who employed the
<>celestial maid Vidyutprabha1 to obstruct the penance of
<>Vis4va1mitra. She came to the forest in which Vis4va1mitra
<>was doing penance and tried to entice the hermit by
<>her beauty. But when she saw that her beauty did not
<>attract the hermit, she assumed a fearful form. Seeing [Page876-a+ 63]
<>this form, the hermit cursed her. “You shall retain this
<>fearful form and live like a giantess.” She requested for
<>redemption. The hermit said that when S4ri1datta, the
<>son of Ka1lanemi, touched her hair she would be re-
<>deemed from the curse.
<NI>After many years Ka1lanemi was born in the country of
<>Ma1lava as the son of a brahmin named Yajn5asena. A
<>son named S4ri1datta was born to this Ka1lanemi. Once
<>S4ri1datta happened to see this giantess in a forest and
<>caught hold of her by the hair. Instantly she got her
<>original form. (Katha1saritsa1gara, Katha1mukhalambaka,
<>Taran3ga 2).
<NI>12) {%Stealing the flesh of a dog.%} Once, at the end of
<>Treta1 Yuga and the beginning of Dva1para Yuga,
<>there was no rain for twelve years. Famine prevailed
<>every-where. The people were in utter want and misery.
<>Hermits left their hermitages and wandered about. In
<>a crowd Vis4va1mitra lost his wife and children and
<>entered a forest and travelled all alone. He entered the
<>hut of a low-caste (Paraya) and begged for food. But
<>none of them even talked to him. He again requested
<>for something to eat. Nobody cared for him. The her-
<>mit fell on the veranda due to weakness.
<NI>Vis4va1mitra saw in the hut some decayed flesh and intes-
<>tine of a dog placed in a corner of the kitchen. He de-
<>cided to steal some of it to appease his hunger. The
<>Can2d2a1las slept when the night advanced. But the lord
<>of the house lay pretending to sleep. Vis4va1mitra slowly
<>entered the kitchen, and opened the pot in which the
<>intestine of the dog was kept. The owner of the house
<>asked, “Who is that?” Vis4va1mitra replied that he had
<>stolen because of his hunger. The eyes of the can2d2a1la
<>were filled with tears because of pity. He said:
<Poem>“Dog is lower than jackal,
<>That is what men say,
<>Of all the parts of its body,
<>the lowest is its posterior.”</Poem>
<NI>Though he said so, he felt glad since he had given
<>Vis4va1mitra food. (M.B. S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 141).
<NI>13). {%Cursing the river Sarasvati1.%} See under Vasis2t2ha,
<>para 2, sub-para 5.
<NI>14) {%Sons.%} Vis4va1mitra had many sons. Their names are
<>given in Chapter 4, Anus4a1sana Parva.
<NI>15). {%Vis4va1mitra and R2gveda.%} R2gveda, Man2dala 5, was
<>composed by the Vis4va1mitra-family. Variations are
<>observed in the two versions of statements about Vis4va1-
<>mitra, occurring in R2gveda and the Pura1n2as. The con-
<>frontations between Vasis2t2ha and Vis4va1mitra occur in
<>R2gveda also. The last four sections of Su1kta 15 of
<>R2gveda, Man2d2ala 3, Anuva1ka 4, are meant to scold
<>Vasis2t2ha. Here Vis4va1mitra curses Vasis2t2ha's family in
<>various ways. In the ‘Annotations of Sa1yan2a’, mention
<>is made that the disciples of Vasis2t2ha freed Vis4va1mitra
<>from the vow of silence, and that instantly these mantras
<>(chants) dawned in his mind. Though the enmity bet-
<>ween Vasis2t2ha and Vis4va1mitra is seen in R2gveda, such
<>elaborate stories as seen in the Pura1n2as do not occur in
<>R2gveda. But Vis4va1mitra procured a prominent place in
<>R2gveda because this hermit rescued Suda1sa from danger
<>and forded him across rivers, and took S4unas4s4epha as
<>his son. Of these two incidents the first is not given
<>much importance in the Pura1n2as. Though the second
<>one occurs in the Pura1n2as, the version is different from [Page876-b+ 64]
<>that of R2gveda. From this it is presumed that the stories
<>taken from R2gveda underwent a thorough change before
<>they appeared in the Pura1n2as.

<>for penance. (Brahma1n2d2a Pura1n2a, Chapter 89).

<HI>VIVA1HA (MARRIAGE).
<NI>1) {%General information.%} In ancient India marriage was
<>considered to be a sacrifice performed in accordance with
<>social customs. Marriage was allowed to those who had
<>completed education at the age of sixteen. (Sama1var-
<>tana). Father or teacher teaches the pupil the Vedas
<>and Veda1n3gas. When the education is completed the
<>teacher or father makes him sit on a seat decorated
<>with flowers, sandalwood etc. and do Goda1navrata. Then
<>he is offered Pan5ca1mr2ta (milk, curd, butter, honey and
<>water). This is called Sama1vartana. With this his
<>brahmacarya ends, and he is allowed to marry and
<>lead the life of a house-holder.
<NI>Marriage is a ceremony with four secondary rites Viz,
<>Kanya1da1na, S4aci1ya1ga, Viva1ha, Caturthi1karman. If the
<>husband is dead, or lost, or has renounced the world,
<>or has become a eunuch or is expelled from society, the
<>woman is allowed to take another husband. If the
<>husband dies, the wife should be given to the brother
<>of the husband. If there is no brother she could accept
<>anybody whom she likes.
<NI>2) {%Eight kinds of marriages.%} The woman and man
<>should not be of the same Gotra (family). One could
<>marry a girl who is above seven generations on the
<>paternal line and above five generations on the mater-
<>nal line. Eight types of marriages allowed in Manu-
<>smr2ti, Chapter 3, are given below:
<NI>(i) {%Bra1hma.%} A man of good qualities and good family
<>is asked to come and receive the damsel. This is
<>Bra1hma. The radiance of this marriage will give the
<>man prosperity.
<NI>(ii) {%A1rs2a.%} After getting a couple of cows from the
<>bridegroom the bride is given to him.
<NI>(iii) {%Pra1ja1patya.%} The virgin is given to the man, who
<>had requested for her hand as a duty.
<NI>(iv) {%Daiva.%} The virgin is offered to the master who is
<>engaged in performing a sacrifice.
<NI>(v) {%Ga1ndharva.%} Marriage between a man and a woman
<>with equal love on either part.
<NI>(vi) {%A1sura.%} Giving money in return for the damsel
<>and marrying her. This type is mean.
<NI>(vii) {%Ra1ks2asa.%} Carrying the damsel away by fight or
<>force.
<NI>(viii) {%Pais4a1ca.%} Marrying a damsel when she is sleeping
<>or lying unconscious.
<HI>VIVARDHANA. A King in ancient India. Mention is
<>made in Maha1bha1rata, Sabha1 Parva, Chapter 4, Stanza
<>21, that this King was a prominent member of the
<>assembly of Yudhis2t2hira. [Page879-a+ 65]
<HI>VIVASVA1N I. The Sun.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} Su1rya (Sun) has a large number
<>of synonyms. But prominence is given to two of them,
<>Ma1rtan2d2a and Vivasva1n in the Pura1n2as. Twelve devas
<>were born to Praja1pati Kas4yapa by his wife Aditi. As
<>these twelve were the sons of Aditi they were called
<>A1dityas. The Dva1das4a1dityas (the twelve A1dityas) are
<>Vis2n2u, S4akra, Aryaman, Dha1ta1, Tvas2t2a1, Pu1s2a1 Vivasva1n,
<>Savita1, Mitra, Varun2a, Am3s4u and Bhaga. These twelve
<>A1dityas were, in the previous Manvantara (Age of
<>Manu) of Manu Ca1ks2us2a, twelve Devas called the
<>Tus2itas. When the Ca1ks2us2a Manvantara came to an
<>end and the Vaivasvata Manvantara was about to
<>begin, the twelve Tus2itas met together and after a con-
<>sultation, they took birth as the sons of Aditi. In this
<>birth they were known by the name Dva1das4a1dityas.
<>(Vis2n2u Pura1n2a, Am3s4a 1, Chapter 15).
<NI>2) {%The name Ma1rtan2d2a.%} As Aditi was pregnant, Candra
<>went to the hermitage asking for alms. Due to her diffi-
<>culties of pregnancy Aditi was not in a position to rise
<>up instantly and greet the visitor. Candra thought that
<>it was due to disrespect. So he cursed her. Let the
<>child in your womb die.” At this Aditi became misera-
<>ble. Kas4yapa saw her crying incessantly and asked for
<>the cause. Aditi told him all that had happened.
<>Kas4yapa blessed her and said that the infant would not
<>die. Thus the child which was lying dead in the womb
<>came to life again. As the ‘an2d2a’ (egg-embryo) of
<>Vivasva1n went mr2ta (died) by the curse of Candra, he
<>came to be called Ma1rtan2d2a (he who has an2d2a which
<>has become mr2ta). When the child was born he was
<>given the name Vivasva1n.
<NI>3) {%Family life.%} Vivasva1n married Sam3jn5a1, the daughter
<>of Vis4vakarma1. The first child born to Vivasva1n by
<>Sam3jn5a1 was Vaivasvata Manu. The Su1rya (Solar)
<>dynasty begins from this Vaivasvata Manu. Sam3jn5a1
<>again gave birth to two children Yama and Yami1. Then
<>finding it difficult to bear the fierce brightness of the
<>sun Sam3jn5a1 gave her place to her maid Cha1ya1 otherwise
<>called Savarn2a1, and went to the house of her father.
<>Vis4vakarma1 did not like this action on the part of his
<>daughter. So Sam3jn5a1 took the form of a mare and went
<>to the pastures of North Kuru. Thinking Cha1ya1 to be
<>his wife Sam3jn5a1, Vivasva1n went to bed with her. She
<>conceived and gave birth to two sons and a daughter.
<>The sons were named Sa1varn2i and S4ani and the daughter
<>was named Tapati1. Cha1ya1 loved her own children more.
<>The children of Sam3jn5a1 were grieved at this. Yama once
<>lifted his leg to kick her. “Let that leg be broken.”
<>Cha1ya1 cursed him. The miserable Yama ran to his
<>father and said. “Father, this mother hates us and loves
<>Sa1varn2i and S4ani more. It is true that I lifted up my
<>leg. But my leg did not touch mother's head. Father, I
<>request you to pardon the wrong I have done because of
<>my ignorance. Have pity on me and tell me how to save
<>my leg from breaking.” Vivasva1n said to Yama that his
<>leg would not be broken, but because of the curse worms
<>would bite his leg. Vivasva1n understood that Cha1ya1
<>was not the real mother. He went to Vis4vakarma1.
<>Vis4vakarma1 put Vivasva1n on his turning machine and
<>by turning lessened his brightness. Vivasva1n who was
<>made more handsome by turning, found out his wife
<>Sam3jn5a1, and approached her. But thinking him to be
<>somebody else she moved away from him. In the mean-
<>while two male persons were born from the nostrils of [Page879-b+ 64]
<>Sam3jn5a1. There is another story that these two persons
<>were the As4vinidevas. Vivasva1n and Sam3jn5a1 came home.
<>As a retribution for the wrong he had done, Yama
<>ruled over his subjects justly and earned the name
<>Dharmara1ja. (Va1mana Pura1n2a, Chapter 21; Bhavis2ya
<>Pura1n2a, Chapter 47; Maha1bha1rata, A1di Parva, Chapter
<>171).
<NI>4) {%Some details about Vivasva1n.%} (i) In Maha1bha1rata,
<>Vana Parva, Chapter 3, the 108 names of Vivasva1n
<>are given.
<NI>(ii) Vivasva1n lived in this world and defeated all his
<>enemies. (M.B. Vana Parva, Chapter 315, Stanza 19).
<NI>(iii) Vivasva1n performed sacrifice in strict accordance
<>with the instructions given in the Vedas and gave as
<>Daks2in2a1 (gift) to the priest, Praja1pati Kas4yapa, the
<>southern quarter. From that day onwards the south
<>got the name Daks2in2adis4a1. (M.B. Udyoga Parva,
<>Chapter 109, Stanza 1).
<NI>(iv) In days of yore Maha1vis2n2u advised Vivasva1n
<>“Anas4varata1karma-yoga”. Vivasva1n advised this art to
<>his son Vaivasvata Manu. (M.B. Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter
<>28, Stanza 1).
<NI>(v) Vivasva1n is included among the twentyeight Pra-
<>ja1patis. (M.B. S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 334, Stanza 36).
<NI>(vi) He learned from Maha1vis2n2u Sa1tvatadharma and
<>taught his son Vaivasvata Manu the same in Treta1yuga.
<>(M.B. S4a1nti Parva, Chapter 348, Stanza 50).
<NI>(vii) The As4vinikuma1ras, Na1satya and Dasra, are the
<>sons of Vivasva1n. They were born through the nose of
<>his wife Sam3jn5a1. (M.B. Anus4a1sana Parva, Chapter 150,
<>Stanza 17).

<HI>VRATA. Controls ordained by Vedic Sam3hita1s are called
<>Vratas. It is known as tapas (penance) also. Vratas

<>the organs of sense is called niyama (control). Vrata,
<>fast and restraining or control are always good. (Agni
<>Pura1n2a, Chapter 175).

<HI>VR2KA I. A son born to Dhr2s2t2aketu, the king of Kekaya

<HI>VR2KA III. An asura. This asura wanted to bring the
<>Devas under his control. “How to achieve it? The only
<>way is to please one of the three god-heads.” The
<>asura saw Na1rada and asked him which of the three
<>god-heads could easily be pleased. Na1rada replied
<>that it was S4iva. Vr2ka resolved to please S4iva and be-
<>gan to do penance. He cut each of his organs and offer-
<>ed it in the fire as oblation. At last when Vr2ka1sura
<>was beginning to cut his head to offer it in fire, S4iva
<>made his appearance, and asked him what his wish
<>was. The boon he requested for, was that any one whose
<>head he touched with his finger should die instantly.
<>S4iva granted that boon.
<NI>The asura decided to try the boon, on the giver himself
<>first. Terrified at this, S4iva began to run. The asura
<>chased him. At last S4iva sought protection from Vis2n2u.
<>Assuming the form of a boy, Maha1vis2n2u stood on the
<>way and stopped Vr2ka1sura, who was running after S4iva.
<>The boy asked him why he was running. The asura
<>told the boy everything. Then the boy laughed and
<>said “Oh! Asura! What S4iva said was a lie. He has no
<>divine power now. He was making fun of you. Not an
<>ant would die by the touch of your fingers. You just try
<>on your head and see for yourself.” Hearing this the
<>asura became dejected. He thought what the boy said
<>was true. The poor creature touched his own head with
<>his finger. The moment he touched his head, he fell
<>down dead. (Bha1gavata, Skandha 10). This story has
<>similarity with that of Bhasma1sura. (See under
<>Bhasma1sura).

<HI>VR2KS2A(S). (TREES). It is stated in Va1lmi1ki Ra1ma1-
<>yan2a, Aran2ya Ka1n2d2a, Sarga 14, Stanza 29, as follows
<>about the origin of Vr2ks2as (trees).
<NI>Praja1pati Kas4yapa married Anala1, the daughter of
<>Daks2a. Trees yielding good fruits were given birth to by
<>Anala1.
<HI>VR2KS2APRATIS2T2HA1. The ancient Indians believed
<>that consecration of Trees and gardens (parks) were
<>means of remission of sins and attainment of heaven. As
<>the consecration of trees is a divine ritual it has to be
<>performed as ordained in the Vedas. The rites are given
<>below:
<NI>As the first item of the consecration ceremony of a tree,
<>besmear it with all kinds of medicinal herbs, and adorn
<>it with flour and flowergarlands and make it wear good
<>clothes. Then make on it perforations for the ears with
<>golden needle, and anoint ointment for eyes with golden
<>wire. Place on the dais prepared at the foot of each
<>tree, seven fruits and pots (Kalas4as) and make invoca-
<>tions. After this, offerings and sacrifices to Indra and
<>the other gods should be given. Again invocation
<>should be made with burnt offerings to Vanaspati. From
<>the middle of the trees alms of cows should be given.
<>Brahmins should bathe the trees with pots placed on the
<>dais, reciting spells and incantations of anointment, and
<>of R2g, Yajur and Sa1ma Vedas along with instrumental
<>music. The owner of the trees should be given bathing
<>water by himself. Then the owner should give cows,
<>lands, ornaments and clothes as gift.
<NI>After having done so much, food with milk should be
<>given for four days and burnt offerings should be made
<>with gingelly etc. and butea. The gift to the priest
<>should be double the gifts given to others. (Agni Pura1n2a
<>Chapter 70).
<HI>VR2KS2AVA1SI1. A Yaks2a. Mention is made in Maha1-
<>bha1rata, Sabha1 Parva, Chapter 10, Stanza 11, that this
<>Yaks2a lives in the palace of Kubera.
<HI>VR2KS2A1YURVEDA. The name Vr2ks2a1yurveda is used for
<>the conventional rules about planting trees near dwel-
<>ling places. According to Vr2ks2a1yurveda it is good to
<>plant Itti (wave-leafed fig-tree) on the North side of
<>the house. Ficus Indica (banyan) should be plantd on
<>the east. Mango tree on the south and Ficus Religiosa
<>(banyan) on the west of the house. Thorny trees should
<>grow up by themselves on the south side of the house.
<>Garden should be close to the house. Sva1ti1, Hasta,
<>Rohin2i1, S4ravan2a and Mu1la are considered to be good
<>stars for planting trees. Stars good for taking trees,
<>across river or in vehicle and to take down into ponds,
<>are Hasta, Magha1, A1rdra1, As4vini1, Pus2yam and Jyes2t2ha1.
<>The stars mentioned above are good for planting Neem
<>tree, Jonesia Asoca, Calophyllum, Mimosasirisha, Acacia
<>Priyan3gu, Syzygium, Mimusops and pomegranate tree.
<>The distance between trees should be twenty rods. This
<>distance is the best. Sixteen rods is medium. But it
<>should never be less than twelve rods. If the tree does
<>not bear fruit, the stem should be examined by cutting
<>with a knife. Then mix powdered vermifuge seeds with
<>ghee and smear it on the cut. Then water the tree. If
<>fruits are destroyed before they ripen, mix the powders [Page881-b+ 64]
<>of horse-gram, black-gram, green-gram, barley and se-
<>sam with ghee and smear the tree and water it. Water-
<>ing the tree with water and ghee will make the tree
<>flower and yield fruits quickly. Mix powdered dung of
<>sheep, powdered Barley, sesam, and cow's flesh with
<>water and keep it for seven days. Then water the tree
<>with this water. This will make any tree yield more fruits
<>and flowers. Watering the trees with fish-water will
<>make them yield fruits more quickly. Mixture of Vermi-
<>fuge seed, fish and rice is a good manure. This manure
<>is a good remedy for all diseases of trees. (Agni Pura1n2a
<>Chapter 281).

<HI>VR2S2A IV. An incarnation of S4iva in the form of an ox.
<>The following is a story that occurs in S4iva Pura1n2a,
<>S4atarudasam3hita1, about this incarnation.
<NI>When the Devas and the Asuras united together
<>and churned the sea of milk, ever so many noble objects

<>Sudars4ana (the weapon of Vis2n2u) and drove him to

<>that day onwards, the world of Pa1ta1la became a for-

<HI>VR2S2ADARBHA I.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} An ancient saintly King in
<>Bha1rata. This King Vr2s2adarbha and another King
<>named Seduka were righteous as well as experts in
<>wielding main and subordinate weapons. After com-
<>pleting the education of Vedas, a brahmin once
<>approached King Seduka and begged as alms some
<>horses for giving gift to his teacher. The Brahmin said
<>“It is my wish that you will give me these horses as
<>alms.” Seduka said that he had not enough wealth or
<>horses to give the teacher's gift. Seduka sent the
<>Brahmin to Vr2s2adarbha. The Brahmin went to Vr2s2a-
<>darbha and begged as alms a thousand horses. The
<>King whipped the Brahmin. He asked the King why he
<>was punished as he had done no wrong. The King
<>asked the Brahmin who was beginning to curse. Ho.
<>Brahmin! Whom are you about to curse? Him who has
<>not given you alms or another Brahmin? The Brahmin
<>said. “O, King I am sent here by Seduka. I
<>begged as he had instructed.”
<NI>The King said. “This evening I shall give you all the
<>tax-collection of this day. You who have been whipped
<>ought not to be sent emptyhanded.” Accordingly the
<>whole of the taxcollection of that day was given to the
<>Brahmin. (M.B. Vana Parva, Chapter 196).
<NI>2) {%Other details.%}
<NI>(i) It is mentioned in Maha1bha1rata, Sabha1 Parva,

<>(M.B. Vana Parva, Chapter 196, Stanza 3).
